First District Association of Rent Reduction Committee Holds Standing Committee Meeting Yesterday

Discussing Various Matters Related to Rent Reduction Implementation

Submitting to Municipal Government and Various Courts for Record

Notifying All Residents to Organize Branch Associations

The First Special District Association of the Municipal Rent Reduction Committee held its first standing committee meeting at the Tianhou Temple Hall yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, discussing various matters related to rent reduction implementation. It submitted a request to the municipal government and various district courts for record, and resolved to notify residents in all alleys to organize branch associations within a limited time, to quickly realize rent reduction. The details are as follows:

Yesterday's Meeting

The association held its first standing committee meeting at the hall at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. The standing committee members present included Ye Qichang, Zhu Zhichun, Wang Honghui, Liu Zhongying, Cai Qiajun, Qiu Jialiang, Qiu Liangyu, Chen Jiufeng, Shen Yuntao, Zhang Dafu, Zheng Dongshan, Zhu Baoluo, Zhou Fuzhang, Zhang Xianfang, and others, totaling more than a dozen people. Chen Jiufeng was elected as chairman, and Zheng Dongshan as recorder. After completing the formalities, the chairman reported on the motions of the previous executive committee meeting and incoming documents from various parties. The following motions were then discussed: (1) The San Duo Li, San Min, Xin Min, You De, Sixth District Branch Associations, and the Fansheng, Baohua, and other Li branch associations of West Huade Road, reported their establishment and requested personnel guidance. Resolved: Handed over to the organization department for handling. (2) The Tenth Branch Association wrote requesting negotiation on the issue of landlords in Shanci Fang increasing water fees. Resolved: Send a letter to the Arnhold & Co. (3) According to the Shanghai Rent Reduction Association's rent reduction measures, the following shall be implemented. Resolved: (A) Announce the rent reduction measures of this district. (B) Each Li branch association shall register with the respective branch association in the area where it is located to establish itself. (4) The Seventh Branch Association wrote stating that Tongchun Li was increasing water fees and requesting negotiation. Resolved: Send a letter to the Tongchang Li property management office. (5) The motion to require district branch associations to actively urge residents of each Li to establish branch associations within a limited time. Resolved: Notify the district association to complete the process within two weeks. (6) The Water and Wood Industry Workers' Union warned the Rent Reduction Association, which is contrary to public opinion, and should be discussed. Resolved: Send a letter of advice. (7) The Ninth Branch Association wrote stating that landlords in Xiangxin Li were oppressing and forcing relocation and requesting assistance. Resolved: (A) Send a letter to the landlord requesting a delay in renovation. (B) Send a letter to the Public Works Department requesting a halt to approvals and protection to ensure residential stability. (8) The Twenty-Sixth Branch Association wrote regarding rent reduction in Yongji, Jiqing, Sanhe, Shunhe Li and Jiangxi Road. Resolved: The branch association shall handle it according to the rent reduction measures of the city association. (9) How to plan for funding. Resolved: Each branch association and branch shall pay a membership fee of five yuan to the district association and report to the city association for record, and notify them separately to facilitate association affairs. (10) How to carry out ordinary rent reduction movements. Resolved: Such as holding a general meeting of resident representatives in the entire district. (11) The motion to set the date for regular meetings. Resolved: Meetings shall be held once a week. (12) The motion that the Xicheng Li rent reduction was met with the landlord sealing the door, and justice should be advocated. Resolved: Send a letter to the Second Special District Association for assistance. The meeting adjourned at 4:30 PM.

Document Submitted to the Municipal Government

The Shanghai Rent Reduction Association submitted documents to the municipal government's Social Affairs Bureau and various courts yesterday, stating: "Submitting this document to revitalize the city, prosper Shanghai, reduce rent, and alleviate the people's livelihood, hoping that you will review and approve the motion to promote this effort quickly to reduce rent, maintain the people's livelihood, and properly plan association affairs. Since the city suffered a tremendous disaster in January 28, 1932, vitality has not yet been restored. The war zone has become a wasteland, and the entire city has become a land of death. The city's condition is deteriorating daily, unemployment is increasing, goods lack markets, and people have no means of survival. The current situation is difficult to sustain, and we cannot afford to consider future troubles. To strengthen the foundation, we must choose what is urgent. Currently, the issue of reducing rent has been forced to become an urgent problem. Landlords and tenants are closely related and should be able to pass through (this difficult time) together. Who would willingly resist? However, there are a few landlords who only know how to benefit themselves and disregard the livelihood of the people. On this day of popular hardship, they have repeatedly increased rents unreasonably. If their desires are not met, they resort to coercion, requesting courts to pursue and detain (tenants) or renovating old houses. Once one landlord initiates such actions, many others follow suit, creating a bad precedent. Among the city's more than three million residents, tenants account for eight or nine out of ten. Reducing clothing and food already requires careful management, and high rents are even more difficult to cope with. Recently, bankruptcies and deaths have been heard of daily, and the main reason is economic hardship. This association was formed by various legitimate groups at the request of all city residents and filed with the city party headquarters and other authorities. A general meeting of representatives also resolved on rent reduction principles as a basis for the rent reduction movement. As for the housing tax, which relates to government expenses, it was also resolved that it should still be paid at the current original amount, so that there is no loss of housing tax, and tenants benefit. Regarding landlords, it was also resolved that all vacant houses must pay housing tax to prevent landlords from holding them up and demanding higher rents. The government can also use this to increase revenue. Regarding landlords, they should also realize that extortion is unreliable. By changing to fair and meager profits, tenants will have lighter burdens, and there will be no worries about renting out vacant houses. The municipal government will also avoid the burden of vacant houses. However, the capitalist mindset does not understand the general trend of people's livelihood and society, arbitrarily making excessive demands, creating a deadlock, causing the people to lose hope of recovery, and the business market is in danger of collapsing. This association's duty lies in speaking frankly and pleading for the people. Therefore, we are submitting this document to the government for review and approval, hoping that you will consider the people's suffering, announce and implement it, and prevent landlords from using the pretext of renovating houses or transferring ownership to increase rents in order to maintain the overall situation and comfort the people. It would truly be a virtuous and convenient act. Respectfully submitted."

Notice to Citizens

"Notice: This association is carrying out the movement to reduce rent in response to the public will of the citizens and the needs of the times. Adjusting the livelihood of the people and stabilizing society lies in this. Rent reduction principles have been resolved by a general meeting of representatives. (Printed separately) Rent shall be paid according to the law, and rent reduction measures shall be handled from January 1934 onwards. If the landlord refuses to accept rent, the rent due shall be deposited in a bank. If tenants have overdue rent up to 1932, it shall be repaid in installments within one year. The rights and interests of rent reduction shall be the same for sub-lessors and sub-tenants. In addition to submitting this document to the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Social Affairs Bureau, and various courts, we hereby give notice."

Chen Lifu Discusses the Government's Purpose in Managing Traditional Chinese Medicine

New Sound News Agency reports that the Shanghai Guanghua Medical and Pharmaceutical Journal Society received a quick letter from its Beijing-based reporter yesterday stating that the central government has a plan to manage traditional Chinese medicine (TCM) which it intends to implement soon. The reporter went to interview Central Committee member Chen Lifu, and asked what the government's purpose was in managing TCM. Chen responded that the government manages TCM to recognize that TCM has thousands of years of history and value, and also because it is concerned about the importance of human life and cannot allow incompetent doctors to kill people at will. Therefore, there must be examinations to distinguish between the good and the bad, and then licenses to practice medicine will be granted. This is the government's purpose in managing TCM. Furthermore, in the future, the government should not be biased towards Western medicine when managing medical affairs, and should not disregard Chinese medicine. The government should vigorously promote research, elucidate, and demonstrate Chinese medicine. The government should also establish specialized agencies to investigate folk remedies and herbs at any time, conduct chemical experiments and provide proof, so that people can have very convenient doctors and very cheap medicines.

Eighteen Bookstores Petition the Authorities to Exempt Books from Prohibition

Commercial Decline Makes Maintenance Difficult

It Inevitably Impairs the Future of Culture

The China Authors and Publishers Association submitted a document to the Central Party Headquarters, the Municipal Party Headquarters, and the Municipal Education Bureau yesterday, stating: "Submitting this document regarding a large number of publications being ordered to be banned and destroyed, requesting a re-examination and lenient treatment to alleviate the plight of businesses and maintain culture. We, the stores, have been engaged in the publishing business in Shanghai for many years. Although it is a for-profit enterprise, we have always sought to contribute to education and promote culture. Therefore, we have always been extremely cautious in publishing books, hoping to avoid harming society or violating laws, thereby harming our own business. Recently, the central government has been very strict in cracking down on publications, and we have become even more vigilant and dare not be negligent. (A) We have followed the provisions of the Publication Law of the Ministry of Interior. (B) On the 19th of this month, officials from your department (Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters) visited our stores in person to verbally announce that we were ordered to prohibit the publication of various publications according to the secret order of the Propaganda Committee of the Central Party Headquarters (your department), and to submit the printed books and printing plates to the department for destruction within a limited time. In total, hundreds of books were investigated and banned, including some that had previously been submitted to the Central Party Headquarters (your department) for review and revision and approved for distribution, some that had been reviewed and registered by the Ministry of Interior and granted publishing copyrights, and some that had been published for many years and had long been considered harmless. We were not notified that these should be banned. The public was terrified and speechless. We believe that the stores are all small businesses. From receiving the manuscript to publishing a book, it takes a year and a half. The investment is no less than four or five hundred gold yuan. Therefore, we must be extremely cautious when printing. We believe that the books that were ordered to be banned this time do not violate the law. Even if it is unavoidable to be negligent, it is only in the words, sentences, or chapters. If the Central Party Headquarters (your department) considers that there are still many violations, if you kindly provide instructions tomorrow and order us to revise, we will be happy to comply. But now, without distinguishing between minor and major offenses, all books are banned and destroyed. At a time of educational decline and commercial depression, the stores are struggling to maintain themselves. This major blow will make it impossible for us to survive. Moreover, in the future, all publishers will be afraid of this severe punishment and will no longer dare to print books, which seems to impair the future of culture. Therefore, we urgently submit this joint petition to your bureau (department), hoping that you will consider the plight of the stores and (forward it to the Central Party Headquarters) for a thorough re-examination of the large number of publications that were banned this time. If there are any chapters or sentences that violate the law, please point them out separately and order the stores to revise them or leave them blank and reprint them to avoid complete destruction. This way, the hard-earned capital of the stores will not be lost, and the central government's intention to correct ideology and crack down on publications will also be seen as more cautious, which will greatly benefit the future of culture. Whether or not this is feasible, we respectfully request your approval and compliance. This would be a virtuous and convenient act. In addition to submitting this to the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters (Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau) (Central Party Headquarters) to forward it, we respectfully submit this to Modern, Nantong, Huatong, Kaiming, Tianma, New Life, Beixin, Liming, United, Asia East, New China, Guanghua, Children, Liangyou, Life, Sanyou, Shenzhou, Guangming and other eighteen bookstores."

Ministry of Military Affairs Issues Red Cross Society Train Tickets

The National Government regards the Chinese Red Cross Society as a charitable organization of the International League of Nations. Last year, the Legislative Yuan formulated and promulgated management regulations, and ordered the Ministries of Military Affairs, Interior, Foreign Affairs, and Navy to jointly draft implementing rules. They stipulated that the treatment of public officials of the Red Cross Society should be the same as that of the military, and that the government should allocate free train and ship tickets for them. Now, according to this plan, the Ministry of Military Affairs has ordered the Transportation Department to allocate military type A and B train tickets to the society for application. It was mailed to the association yesterday, it is said.

The Japanese newspaper Daily News reported that the Korean independence movement has a history of sixteen years since its occurrence. After the so-called provisional government was established, it carried out active secret activities, contacted internal and external parties, and expanded the resistance front. According to news from the Chinese side, the responsibility for the arrests in the January 28 and April 29 incidents lay with the leaders. At the same time, Zhao Suang was elected as the Minister of Internal Affairs, Kim Kyusik as the Minister of Foreign Affairs, Yin Qixie as the Minister of Military Affairs, Choi Dongmu as the Minister of Justice, and Song Yongxi as the Minister of Finance.

The original purpose of the aviation donation was to purchase airplanes for consolidating air defense. Moreover, the airplanes purchased with these funds are often named after the donors to commemorate and encourage them. Recently, according to a report in this newspaper on the 13th of this month, the Ministry of Railways telegraphed the Ping-Han Railway Bureau, stating that railway workers purchased ten airplanes, two of which went to Wuhan and were named 'Ping-Han' Numbers 1 and 2, to comfort the workers' expectations. Furthermore, the other eight airplanes are all named 'Railway,' which is one example. Our national postal workers' aviation donation amounts to 300,000 yuan. In terms of patriotic donations, we are not behind anyone. Our union has repeatedly submitted requests to the Ministry of Communications and sent letters to your directorate, suggesting that the central competent authority quickly purchase airplanes and name them 'Postal Worker' to maintain credibility and meet the public's expectations, which are all on record. However, up to this day, it has not been implemented. Our union and postal workers across the country strongly disapprove of this donation being used for other purposes. In addition to submitting a report to the Ministry, we are sending this letter to your directorate, requesting you to quickly forward it to the competent authority for implementation, to maintain our public relationship." This is addressed to the Directorate General of Posts. (The text submitted to the Ministry of Communications is similar and omitted).

New Shanghai-Beiping Passenger Train to Make Its First Trip Tomorrow Evening

Railway Bureau Announces Value and Numbers

After the renovation of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, a new Shanghai-Beiping passenger train was completed. It passed the gate test drive well and is scheduled to make its first trip as the 302nd Shanghai-Beiping train tomorrow afternoon at 12:00 noon. The Railway Bureau announced yesterday the approximate value of the entire Shanghai-Beiping passenger train: four newly built carriages: 177,000 yuan (i.e., the number used this time); old chassis for four newly built carriages: 55,300 yuan; six original carriages, carriage bodies: 121,400 yuan; six original carriages, chassis: 82,900 yuan, totaling 436,600 yuan.

Jianghai Customs Proclamation Amends Regulations on Ordinary Goods

Effective March 1st

Jianghai Customs issued Proclamation No. 1335 yesterday, stating, "Now, according to the government's order, Article 18 of the Regulations on Ordinary Goods Customs Procedures shall be amended as follows: Article 18: Merchants who wish to withdraw goods from warehouses and transport them overseas shall first submit a declaration for the re-export of goods withdrawn from warehouses and transported overseas, and provide a guarantee, ensuring that if the goods are found to be in violation of regulations, they will pay up to ten times the amount of tax assessed by the customs within the period stipulated by customs. Only after the customs verifies that the declaration matches the goods will a permit for the re-export of goods withdrawn from warehouses and transported overseas be issued, and the goods released. If a merchant obtains a permit, withdraws the goods from the warehouse, and then fails to transport all or part of the goods to a ship for export, the customs may execute the guarantee provided by the merchant and order the merchant to pay the tax that should have been levied on the goods listed in the permit. If, when the goods are loaded onto the ship, the customs finds that all or part of the goods do not match the goods listed in the permit, or if the goods have been loaded onto the ship and transported, and then secretly unloaded at other places in China, with the intention of evading taxes, the customs may execute the full amount of the guarantee. Merchants who withdraw goods from warehouses and transport them under bond to other treaty ports shall first submit a declaration for the withdrawal of goods from warehouses under bond for re-export to other treaty ports, and provide a guarantee, ensuring that if the goods are not declared for import at the customs of the designated port of destination according to the usual procedures, the merchant shall pay the import taxes. Only after the customs verifies that the declaration matches the goods will a permit for the re-export of goods withdrawn from warehouses and transported under bond to other treaty ports be issued, and the goods released. If a merchant obtains a permit, withdraws the goods from the warehouse, and then fails to load the goods onto the ship specified in the permit for export, the customs may handle the matter according to the guarantee. As for returned goods, regardless of whether they were originally declared for transport overseas or to other treaty ports when they were withdrawn from the warehouse, merchants may withdraw the goods after paying the import taxes, or store the goods back in the customs warehouse, as they see fit. However, the 12-month storage period shall still be calculated from the date of the initial entry into the warehouse. These procedures for issuing guarantees for the transport of goods shall take effect on March 1, 1934. From that date onward, all goods withdrawn from customs warehouses must be handled according to these procedures. All merchants are hereby ordered to comply. This proclamation is hereby issued."

Match Industry Plans to Establish Seven-Province Joint Distribution Office

The Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Match Industry Coordination Association convened its third meeting of the three-province industry representatives yesterday afternoon to discuss relief measures. The attending representatives included Sun Runzhai from the Shanghai China Factory, Shao Xiushan from the Daming Factory, Gao Songfu from the Dahua Factory, Xu Jingzhi from the Ningbo Zhengda Factory, and Xu Guangji from the Linhuai Huaishang Factory, totaling more than ten people. As a result, they plan to continue requesting the government to appropriately reduce tax rates and asking for assistance from all sectors. Dispute Resolved Over Small Sanbei Steamship

Reinstated Workers Have Boarded and Resumed Service

A dispute arose over the change of route of the Small Sanbei Steamship of the China Merchants Sanbei Steamship Company and the resulting reduction of middle-class workers. The Preparatory Committee of the Chinese Seamen's Union, fearing an incident, determined a temporary solution at the time, temporarily ordering half of the workers to remain on board, while the remaining half waited for negotiations with the company to resume work. After several negotiations, the Seamen's Union negotiated with the company's manager, Yu Qiaqing, and a resolution was reached immediately. The solution was that of the original 25 middle-class workers who were union members, three would be laid off, and all six workers who were not union members would be dismissed. The reinstated workers immediately boarded the ship and resumed their normal duties.

March 10th at 10:00 AM

Improving Shanghai's Police

The Municipal Government Asks Li Wanli to Undertake the Design

The Public Safety Bureau Forms a Police Reorganization Committee

Mayor Wu, believing that the city's police districts were established twenty years ago and are no longer suitable due to municipal improvements in recent years, has specially invited police expert Li Wanli to undertake the improvement design and has instructed him on the following improvement directions: (1) Shanghai's financial resources are stretched and cannot exceed the original budget; (2) To enable the police to be proactive and conscientious, attention must be paid to patrol areas, with one police officer assigned to each area to be responsible for all police duties; (3) To make it clear to the public, all Public Safety Bureau offices must be named after the local place name, abolishing the terms "First" and "Second." Mr. Li has now, based on the directions given by the Mayor and with reference to principles and actual conditions, begun the design. The Public Safety Bureau has also dispatched Inspector Cheng Fengyi to accompany Mr. Li on a survey of the terrain to facilitate the demarcation of districts. To promote cooperation, the Public Safety Bureau Director, Jiao Hongen, has specially gathered the bureau's commissioned police officers and organized a police reorganization committee, and has invited Mr. Li to participate to avoid gaps and promote harmony.

Fearing a Resurgence of Gambling During the Lunar New Year

Strict Arrests Will Be Made for Those Who Dare to Violate

The Director of the Shanghai Public Safety Bureau, Wen Hongen, fearing gambling and profiteering during the Lunar New Year, has specifically re-enforced the ban. The original text of the proclamation is as follows: Gambling and profiteering are not only detrimental to morality but also affect the livelihood of ordinary people and should be severely punished according to the law. Orders have been repeatedly issued to prohibit them, but unfortunately, with the passage of time, people become complacent and repeat the same mistakes. Ignorant people often exhaust the fruits of their year-long labor, throwing it all away in a single gamble, even mortgaging and borrowing to try to win. If they win, they indulge in pleasure without restraint and become dissolute. If they lose, they become discouraged and lose their spirit, unable to sustain their lives. At best, they waste time and lose their jobs. At worst, they are ruined and their families are destroyed. Harmony is lost in the family, and disasters arise from this, directly harming the family and indirectly harming society. Now that the Lunar New Year is approaching, there is a fear of a resurgence of gambling. At a time when the economy is declining and resources are scarce, all our citizens should not waste any more of their mental or financial resources. This bureau, in charge of public safety, is responsible for banning gambling. Therefore, a proclamation is hereby issued to reiterate the warnings, urging people from all walks of life to comply and refrain from gambling. Those who dare to violate will be strictly arrested. As for teahouses that engage in gambling and profiteering, in addition to being arrested according to the law, they will be ordered to close down without leniency. Be warned. This proclamation is hereby issued.

Female Headmaster Sues Female Teacher's Father-in-Law

For Hiding His Daughter-in-Law and Preventing Her From Coming to School

And Assaulting Her When She Went to Question Him

The Judge Hopes Both Parties Will Try to Reconcile

Zhuo Jiezhen, a Guangdong woman and headmaster of Baocui Elementary School in Tianfuli, Elqin Road, recently hired lawyer Chen Nan to file a lawsuit in the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court against Zhong Yaolao, a Cantonese man and owner of the Haoshilai Food Store on Jielu Road, for restricting freedom. The facts of her lawsuit are as follows: Zhuo founded Baocui Elementary School in 1928 and has been running it for six years. When school started on January 13th of this year, she hired Zhong Rong's daughter-in-law, Zhong Qu Yue'e, a Cantonese woman and daughter of Qu Yueshan, to serve as a first-grade teacher. Unexpectedly, after only half a month, Yue'e took a day off on January 29th and then another day off on the 30th. By the 31st, she still had not come to school, causing classes to be suspended. However, because the school had only recently started, the suspension of classes was affecting the school and the children's studies. Therefore, on February 1st, she questioned Qu Yueshan, the introducer, and asked her to inquire with the defendant. Zhuo then went with her husband, Tan Qingpu, to the defendant's place to urge Yue'e to come to school. Unexpectedly, the defendant not only hid Yue'e upstairs, preventing her from seeing them, but also detained Zhuo in the store, inciting the shop assistants to arbitrarily assault and humiliate her, restricting her freedom of movement for about two hours. He then falsely accused Zhuo of abducting his daughter-in-law, Yue'e, and took her to the police station. After clarifying the matter, they ordered Zhuo to go home. The defendant's actions constitute the crimes of restricting freedom and defaming reputation under Articles 316 and 330 of the Criminal Law, and therefore a lawsuit is filed, along with a private suit, requesting compensation for the losses incurred. The court approved the lawsuit and ordered a hearing for yesterday afternoon. Judge Liu Yugui presided over the hearing in Criminal Court No. 8. The defendant did not appear, and lawyer Wu Shaoshan appeared on his behalf, stating that the defendant was ill due to his age and being upset, so he could not appear in court today and requested an adjournment. Judge Liu briefly questioned the plaintiff, Zhuo Jiezhen, about her age and hometown. Since both parties are formal merchants and the lawsuit arose from a school dispute, to resolve the matter peacefully, he advised the lawyers of both parties to go out and try to reconcile. The case was adjourned for further hearing on the afternoon of the 27th.

Ministry-Determined Principles for Calculating Long and Short Route Transportation Costs for Intermodal Goods

The two railway bureaus received instructions from the Ministry of Railways yesterday stating that, according to a case presented by the Intermodal Transport Office, the Railway and Longhai Railway Traffic Offices sent a telegram to the Intermodal Transport Office regarding the transportation of 40 tons of soap from Shanghai Station, specifying that it was to be transported via Jinpu and Beining to Shijiazhuang. However, the Xuzhoufu Station on the Jinpu Railway mistakenly transferred it to the Longhai Railway, resulting in a change of route. Due to the different refund and deduction of intermodal transport costs and the different basic freight rates of each railway, the shorter route had higher transportation costs, while the longer route had lower transportation costs. The loss of the Beining Railway was not enough to offset the gain of the Longhai Railway, resulting in insufficient distribution of the original transportation costs and requiring the merchant to pay the difference. The Ministry has now decided on the following principles: (1) For goods that can travel the same origin and destination via two routes, if the mileage of the route designated by the merchant is longer but the transportation cost is lower, and the purpose is solely to reduce transportation costs, the railway should charge the transportation cost of the shorter route and still transport it via the shorter route. (2) The transportation cost collected for the shorter route should be distributed to the actually transporting railways according to the proportion of transportation costs that each railway should receive. According to the above principles, the transportation cost of the 40 tons of soap should still be calculated according to the route via Jinpu and Beining, and no additional transportation costs should be collected from the merchant. The above transportation costs should be distributed among the Jinghu, Jinpu, Longhai, and Pinghan railways according to the proportion of transportation costs that each railway should receive. The staff at the Xuzhoufu Station on the Jinpu and Longhai railways who made the mistake of transferring the soap freight cars should be warned so that they pay attention to the route filled in on the freight ticket and car plate when transferring freight cars in the future. The originating station should also find a way to specially indicate the route of such freight cars on the car plate and the envelope containing the freight ticket to facilitate identification by the connecting station. In addition to issuing the industry to the clearing division of the Intermodal Transport Office to handle according to the above principles in the freight intermodal transport account for that month and ordering separately, it is hereby ordered to comply. The bureau has forwarded this order to the Traffic Office for compliance.

Summary of Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department Budget

After Review by the Board of Directors

It Was Still Submitted to the Finance Committee for Review

The draft budget for the Shanghai Municipal Council's Health Department for this year was submitted to the Board of Directors for review on February 21st. It was still submitted to the Finance Committee for review. Under the temporary expenses item, as usual, the various sub-items were marked with the letters A, B, and C. Items marked with A were already approved or considered urgent needs, while items marked with C were those that should not be paid this year due to financial or other reasons. The temporary expenses included some provisions for land acquisition, so that they could be purchased when the opportunity arose and improve the condition of public land. In addition, the results of the consideration of various construction costs are as follows:

Slaughterhouse Construction

The final payment for the construction of the new slaughterhouse is 50,000 yuan, and the final payment for equipment is 10,000 yuan, both marked with the letter A. The construction cost of the meat market and cold storage is 250,000 yuan, and the equipment cost is reduced to 280,000 yuan, both marked with the letter B. The expansion cost of the Huasheng Road pig slaughterhouse is 35,000 yuan, marked with the letter C. The partial construction cost of the new pig slaughterhouse planned to be built in the East District is 50,000 yuan, because the asphalt manufacturing machine must be moved first, the reduction is 5,000 yuan, marked with the letter A.

Hospital Construction

A draft plan has been prepared for the mental hospital, and the construction cost has been reduced to 100,000 yuan, marked with the letter A. The final payment for the Victoria Nurses' Home is 10,000 yuan. The construction cost of the Western District Fever Hospital has been reduced to 200,000 yuan because the address has not yet been selected, marked with the letter A. The reconstruction of the foreign isolation hospital will not begin until the new fever hospital is completed, and the nominal fee is 100 yuan, marked with the letter C. The ordinary hospital will not begin until the existing Chinese isolation hospital is demolished, and the nominal fee is 100 yuan, also marked with the letter C. There is also a residence for nurses, and the nominal construction cost is 100 yuan, also marked with the letter C.

Vegetable Market Construction

The Dong Hongkou vegetable market will be rebuilt with cement at a cost of 80,000 yuan. The Huishan Road vegetable market is considered urgently needed, and its cost will be reduced to 140,000 yuan. The above two items are marked with the letter "A." The reconstruction of the Avenue Road vegetable market is hindered by existing business, with a nominal fee of 100 yuan marked with the letter "C." The expansion of the Xiaoshadu Road vegetable market should be delayed, costing 80,000 yuan and marked with the letter "C." The Hongkou vegetable market plans to convert existing bungalows into three-story buildings at an estimated cost of one million yuan. As this may interfere with existing operations, it is proposed to wait until the new meat market is completed before further discussion, with a nominal fee of 100 yuan marked with the letter "C." The Beijing Road vegetable market will have a third-floor roof added and a freight elevator installed for 100,000 yuan, marked with the letter "C." The expansion of the Xinzha vegetable market is pending the acquisition of land. Wooden partitions will be added to Machao Road, North Fujian Road, Pingliang Road, and other locations. All of these expenses are marked with the letter "C."

Open-Air Swimming Pool

The open-air swimming pool plans to expand the men's changing room, requiring 7,000 yuan. However, as the pool is already very crowded, it is generally believed that it is better to build a new pool instead of spending more money here. This item is marked with the letter "C." Regarding the construction of a new pool, it will be discussed after the Director of Public Works submits an investigation report.

Sanitation Branch

The Health Department plans to build a third eastern branch office on Zhoushan Road, costing 7,000 yuan, marked with the letter "D." The first northern branch office costs 45,000 yuan, the second eastern branch office costs 15,000 yuan, and the first western branch office costs 27,000 yuan. These figures are all marked with the letter "C."

Other Construction

The Pudong Cemetery will be fenced with wire mesh at a cost of 3,500 yuan, marked with the letter "A." Minor repairs to the Jing'an Temple cemetery will cost 1,500 yuan, marked with the letter "A." Construction and equipment costs for the laundry are each 30,000 yuan, both marked with the letter "A." A nominal fee of 100 yuan, marked with the letter "C," will be used to build an injectable experimental laboratory in the Eastern District. As for recurring expenses, excluding material costs and various donations, the original listed amount exceeded the previous year by 160,000 yuan. After review and reduction, the excess amount was reduced to 78,730 yuan, bringing the total to 1,683,990 yuan, an increase of 4.9% compared to the previous year. The main reason for the increase is the recurring maintenance costs of the new slaughterhouse and the management fees for food and milk. Furthermore, the examination of students' physical condition, based on the results of a pilot program in a certain school, is considered very important. However, this plan has not yet been formally approved by the Board of Directors, so this matter will be left for further discussion at the next Health Committee meeting.

Establishing a Police Officer Training Institute

Should be handled according to the Ministry's regulations.

Internal communication to the Municipal Government for review.

The Ministry of Interior believes that although there are many police officer training institutes established in various provinces and cities, many have not been fully managed in accordance with the Ministry's regulations, resulting in inconsistencies and poor results. In order to rectify this situation, the Ministry has issued a general notice to all provinces and cities, requiring them to pay attention to the following points when establishing police officer training institutes in the future. (1) Supervise the establishment, restore those that have been suspended, and manage those that have been established in accordance with the Ministry's regulations, without making excuses for suspension. (2) Review and approve textbooks to ensure uniformity. (3) Enforce strict training to cultivate excellent character. (4) Enforce the practice of martial arts to strengthen the body and promote the spirit of chivalry embodied in martial arts. (5) Carefully select teachers. (6) Add Chinese language courses, etc., to achieve unification and promote improvement.

The China Cotton Cloth Market Actively Promotes the Unified Control Work

Selecting basic weaving households and rewarding the best ones.

The China National Cotton Cloth Market, in order to promote the sales of domestic yarn and gradually unify the cotton cloth business, is actively promoting it according to the planned plan and spare no effort. It is recently learned that in order to increase production and stabilize the work of weaving households, the market has selected several weaving households registered with the Production Guidance Committee of the market as basic weaving households, temporarily limited to 2,000 looms, and will gradually expand to achieve unification. The yarn used by these basic weaving households will be purchased by the market at the market price, without additional charges. If the performance is excellent, awards will be given according to the award standards to show encouragement. In this way, not only will the work of small weaving households be stabilized and the products improved, but also the entire unified control plan will be gradually implemented.

National Invention of Water-Powered Motor

Submitting to the National Government Again Requesting Assistance

Mr. Shan Chunqiao and Mr. Chen Xinbiao from Zhejiang, after successfully inventing the water-powered motor (i.e., the self-powered engine) last year, aroused the attention of all circles at home and abroad. However, the inventors' application to the central government for approval to guarantee patent rights has not been approved by the relevant department for more than a year. Therefore, it cannot be officially opened. Recently, it has been heard that the inventors, due to the difficulty of delaying the matter any further, have submitted another document to the National Government and the Ministry of Industry. The original submission is recorded as follows:

Document to the National Government

Submitting a request for assistance in the invention of a self-powered engine in order to achieve complete success and practical application. The people have spent more than ten years of effort and sacrificed all kinds of spiritual and economic resources to invent a kind of "self-powered engine" that does not require any fuel consumption and only needs a small amount of water to start the machine wheel, which rotates freely. Its power is equal to that of motors and engines that use electricity, kerosene, and other fuels, and even surpasses them. The people originally planned to manufacture the entire engine and open it to the public for testing. However, the production of the entire engine to practical use requires thousands of gold pieces. The people have sacrificed too much in research, resulting in a violation of their wishes. They are willing to stop in the middle of the road, and all their life's efforts have been paid to the east. Therefore, on the 4th of this month, they submitted a detailed document to the government, requesting practical assistance. After more than ten days, they have not received any good news. They hereby submit another document to the government requesting assistance. This matter concerns the invention of the Chinese people. It is hoped that it will be approved immediately. They are extremely eager to wait for orders. Respectfully submitted to the Chairman of the National Government, Lin, by Chen Xinbiao and Shan Chunqiao.

Document to the Ministry of Industry

Submitting a request for prompt protection of the self-powered engine. The people have invented a kind of "self-powered engine" that does not require any fuel consumption and only needs a small amount of water to start the machine wheel, which rotates freely. Its power is equal to that of motors and engines that use electricity, kerosene, and other fuels, that is, the existing specialized leading types, and the size of the specialization is the same according to its needs, and its advantages surpass them. It has been successfully announced and published in various newspapers. The people originally planned to make the entire engine to meet the needs. Now, because they have not obtained sufficient protection from the Ministry, it is inconvenient to present it rashly. In addition, in the process of research, they have worked hard and failed more than a hundred times over more than ten years, resulting in too much sacrifice. Therefore, they have violated their wishes. Therefore, in November of last year, they prepared a document and attached drawings and instructions, submitting it to the Central Industrial Experiment Institute of the Ministry, requesting a fair evaluation and the issuance of a certificate so that they could raise funds to complete the entire engine and make it practical. Although they have submitted several documents, they have never received a reply, which is very incomprehensible. Now, the establishment of the preparatory office has been long overdue, and the economy is exhausted. It is difficult to delay the matter any further, and the villains are imitating it. It is impossible to submit to the government, requesting assistance, hoping that you will be concerned about the difficulties. This matter concerns the invention of the Chinese people. At this critical moment, I sincerely hope that you will approve it immediately. I am extremely eager to wait for orders. Respectfully submitted to Minister of Industry Chen Junjian by Chen Xinbiao and Shan Chunqiao.

Fire at the Qimei Road Bridge in Zhabei

Burning Down Six Straw Houses, Five Families

The Qimei Road Bridge area in Zhabei is inhabited by poor people who live in thatched huts and work as rickshaw pullers. The Municipal Public Security Bureau's Household Registration Section has not numbered the houses. At around 11:00 PM the night before last, a fire broke out at the house of Lu Liu due to carelessness. In an instant, clouds of smoke filled the area and quickly spread to the roof. When the nearby police learned of the fire, they immediately notified the Zhabei fire brigades in various sections and dispatched fire trucks to rush to the scene to extinguish the fire with all their might. After about an hour, the fire was extinguished, but six thatched huts, including five families, were burned down. The scene was very chaotic. The chief of the fifth district and third precinct of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Wen Yizeng, sent police to suppress the chaos, maintain order, and investigate the cause of the fire. The fire starter, Lu Liu, was taken to the station for questioning.

The Shishi Xinbao Held its Fourth Shareholders' Meeting Yesterday

Amending the Articles of Association and Re-electing the Current Board of Directors and Supervisors

The Shishi Xinbao held its fourth shareholders' meeting at the Bankers' Association at 5:00 PM yesterday. Out of 2,000 shares, 1,879 were present. Out of a total of 1,650 voting rights, 1,539 were present. First, Chairman Xu Xinliu presided over the opening ceremony as usual. Then, General Manager Zhang Zhuping reported on the business conditions in 1933, stating that the paper's business progress last year had broken new records, more than doubling the business income in 1930, etc. Then, Supervisor Zheng Yaonan reported on the accounts and the attached resolutions were passed. Then, the amendment of the Articles of Association was discussed. The number of directors was increased from seven to nine, and the term of office was changed from three years to one year. The reserve fund was changed from 10% to 30%, and the shareholder dividend was reduced from 60% to 40%. The attached resolutions were unanimously passed. Then, the directors were re-elected. As a result, nine directors were elected: Xu Xinliu received 1,509 voting rights, Zhang Gongquan received 1,190 voting rights, Dai Gengxin received 1,529 voting rights, Cheng Linsheng received 1,529 voting rights, Yu Zuoting received 1,524 voting rights, Zhang Zhuping received 1,287 voting rights, Pan Gongbi received 1,435 voting rights, Wang Yingbin received 1,377 voting rights, and Xiong Shaoquan received 1,460 voting rights. Dong Guanzhen, received 1,516 voting rights, and Zheng Yaonan, 1,325 voting rights, were elected as supervisors.

Kun Opera Preservation Society's Successful Performance

The Kun Opera Preservation Society's second performance, yesterday was the first night. Before 8 o'clock, both the upper and lower seats were full. The first play was Qiao Zhijun's "Night Flight," with agile movements and steady postures. The second was Xu Liecheng's "Yunyang Dharma Field," a work that emphasized both singing and acting, and was performed flawlessly from beginning to end. Wang Yimin's "Cui Shi" was effortless and full of color. Pang Jingzhou and Gu Chuanjie's "Questioning and Exploring" were excellent. Ding Zhixiang and Zhang Zhaocheng's "Linked Rings: Small Feast" were one brave and extraordinary, the other mature and deeply calculating. Wang Fumin's "Chopping E" was a Zhengdan leading role, with extremely heavy singing. Mr. Wang's words were clear and his voice was mournful, making him a prominent figure. Xiang Xinwu's "Good Date" was well-known for its strengths. The "Twelve Reds" section had delicate singing and flexible movements, making it an excellent combination of singing and dancing. Yin Zhenxian assisted him with his skills as a veteran craftsman, making it a perfect match. Zhang Zidong's "Beat the Gong" contained sadness within strict restraint, making the audience feel sad and worthy of an old writer. The Yao brothers cooperated with him, making it even more impressive. The finale, "Peony Pavilion," featured Mei Lanfang's Du Liniang, with the beautiful scenery of "Wandering in the Garden" and the charming drowsiness of "Dream of Awakening." He portrayed a heartbroken young woman who was injured in the spring vividly and delicately. The art of the play was to its peak. Yu Zhenfei's Liu Mengmei was extremely affectionate, with a graceful demeanor and a melodious voice, unmatched at the time. Qin Wangjie's Chunxiang was a vivid and innocent girl of thirteen or fourteen years old, charming and lovable. Wang Detian, Pan Xiangsheng, Qin Tongli, and Zhang Zhaocheng also cooperated well. With such a wonderful program, no wonder the audience was never tired. Tonight is the second day of the performance, with Mei Lanfang and Yu Zhenfei performing "Broken Bridge and Yaotai" as a double performance. Other plays are also more exciting, and the grand occasion will surely be even better.

The Wuhan Municipal Government Bans the Dadong Textbook

The Dadong Bookstore in this city, due to the publication of a natural science textbook that damaged the reputation of the telegraph, aroused the public anger of the telegraph bureau staff. The Hankou Telegraph Bureau has also filed a request with the Hankou Municipal Government for review. The Hankou Municipal Government, because the textbook is based on fiction and violates the facts, is enough to harm children and damage the reputation of state-owned enterprises. It has approved the request of the Hankou Telegraph Bureau and ordered all schools not to purchase the textbook.

The Contribution of Dazhong Laundry Company to Women

Mr. Wu Yafei, director of the business department of Dazhong Laundry Company at No. 18, opposite the Postal Bureau on North Sichuan Road in this city, after inventing the solid-quality washing and dyeing method last year, has been recognized by all circles as an unprecedented contribution to the washing and dyeing industry in our country. Therefore, the company's business has also greatly advanced, and its achievements have exceeded the budget. However, in order to combine with all circles and publicize the quality, theory, and technology of this method, Mr. Wu has specially set up five departments: consultant, research, communication, training, and collection and delivery, in order to promote the convenience of service to all circles. At the same time, a kind of postcard with the company's address printed on it is available for customers without telephones to communicate with, and can be obtained at any time. Mr. Wu is currently continuing to study various scientific washing and dyeing methods in order to make his products reach the best and most beautiful state. It is now heard that Mr. Wu, in view of the current fashionable women's coats, which are popular with hard collars, but once washed, their fluffy nature is completely lost, and the texture becomes hairy, making it impossible to restore them, deeply regrets this. Therefore, he has devoted himself to research, spending more than five months of effort, and finally used chemical methods to invent a non-acidic, pure, and clean gelatin. After washing and dyeing, applying this glue not only makes the clothes look like new, but also keeps the texture unchanged. Therefore, it can be used for washing and dyeing new cheongsams and other clothes.

Preparations to Commemorate Qian Zhenya

Mr. Qian Zhenya, professor of sociology at Shanghai Hujiang University and president of the Hudong Commune, unfortunately passed away some time ago due to excessive bleeding after a tooth extraction, despite medical treatment. Various organizations in Shanghai, remembering Mr. Qian's lifelong dedication to social work and his illustrious achievements, have initiated a memorial service to honor his memory. The first preparatory meeting was held yesterday at the Shanghai University Alumni Association in the Continental Emporium. Representatives from over ten organizations attended, including Fan Zhengkang from Hujiang University, Zhang Chunjiang and Weng Shouren from Hudong Commune, Wu Zelin from the Chinese Sociological Society, Chen Zhengfan from the Chinese Children's Welfare Association, Jin Longzhang and Wang Zhiya from the Xing Society, and Deng Yuzhi from the Young Women's Christian Association. It was decided that the memorial service would be held on March 10th at the auditorium of the YMCA on Sichuan Road. The four organizations, Hujiang University, Hudong Commune, Xing Society, and the Shanghai University Alumni Association, were jointly elected as the executive committee of the preparatory committee, responsible for all matters related to the preparation of the memorial service. An office was set up within the Shanghai University Alumni Association on the fourth floor of the Continental Emporium on Nanjing Road to facilitate communication.

Letters to the Editor

To the Esteemed Editor:

Respectfully, regarding the article "A Fierce Battle in a Robbery of a Bride" published in your newspaper on the 18th of this month, upon verification, many of the facts are inconsistent. According to the report submitted by the Sixth Jia of our regiment, the bride robbery was a personal action by Yan Quansheng. This Jia did not have any regimental soldiers, personnel, or firearms mixed in. Furthermore, according to the report of the Eighth, while on patrol that night, they heard news of a bride robbery at the Kang family's residence in the territory and immediately rushed to stop it, detaining Yan Guixu, Yan Jinsheng, Yan Meisheng, Qian Shengrong, and other four relatives of Yan Quansheng on the spot. After inquiries, it was found that there were no other circumstances, and they were released together. There was no fierce battle with any team. Based on this, we respectfully submit this letter for correction, hoping that you will take note and publish it in the Letters to the Editor section to clarify the facts. With best wishes,

The Second District Regiment Headquarters of the Baoshan County Defense Regiment.

Reading Q&A

Translation Clarification

Reading Guidance:

Seeing that your library has established this column in the newspaper makes me unspeakably happy. Although I am not a reading member of your library, and although I live in such a remote countryside, I am very fortunate: while reading the "Shen Bao," I can get a free ride. So, gentlemen, I picked up my pen and wrote this letter.

Undoubtedly, the creation of your column is worthy of praise for the current Chinese cultural movement, and it is also urgently needed! However, I feel that there are still a few points: 丨 But perhaps this is just "superfluous"!

1. In discussing scientific theories, be bold and clearly instruct the questioner.

2. When discussing reading methods or indicating reference books, I also hope to pay attention to "concrete application" and avoid abstract jargon.

3. Expand the length.

Below, I write out my questions: 丨

1. In the Japanese translation of "Das Kapital" (Capital) (translated by Takaseki, published by Kaizosha in Showa 7th year), on page 15 of the original author's second edition preface, the second sentence of line 15: (　　　現存　事　態　光明　　　　　　　　　　　　　如　見元　　　　　　). In other Chinese translations of dialectics, it is mostly translated as "confusing reality," only one person has translated it as: defending the existing (roughly like this, please see Wang Lingao's translation of Hegel's "Outline of the Philosophy of History," translator's preface). I do not understand German, I do not know what the original meaning of this sentence is, please gentlemen analyze it.

2. Is there a Chinese translation of Hegel's "Science of Logic"? Zhou Gucheng's "Outline of Logic," which was recently advertised in the newspaper, is it its complete translation? What is the price?

3. Is "Small Logic" another name for "Encyclopedia of Philosophical Sciences"? Alright, I'll come again next time!

Finally, I must say "me." I am a student of a vocational school who is under twenty years old and will soon graduate. I am very interested in social sciences, and I hope to often receive guidance from you. (Deng Baofu)

The following is a reply to the suggestions in the letter:

1. In principle, I completely agree: but I can only do it within the scope of our ability and "the possibility of facts."

2. The "Reading Q&A" column is only part of the work of this department, that is, the discussion of general reading problems. All those that are convenient for individual replies are not inserted, so some people say that we talk too generally, and there is a suspicion of being unspecific. In fact, this is only seeing a part. Of course, even when discussing general issues, we should also try to avoid completely abstract empty talk.

3. Whether the "Reading Q&A" column can be further expanded depends on the development of our work. The following is the answer to the few points you asked.

4. Regarding the sentence in "Das Kapital" (Capital): 『曾　　現存　事　態　光明　　　　　　　　如　見元　　　　　　』I don't have the German text at hand. According to the English translation by Samuel Moore and Aveling (this English translation is very reliable), the sentence corresponding to this one is...Because it seemed to transfigure and to glorify the existing state of things… It should be translated as "Because it (referring to taking the mystified dialectic, that is, Hegel's dialectic) seems to beautify and brighten the existing things." And theoretically, it must be like this to be consistent with the context. Translating it as "defending..." is not very appropriate, and if it is translated as "confusing...", it is simply incomprehensible.

5. "Small Logic" is part of the "Encyclopedia of Philosophical Sciences," this is in relation to Hegel's "Great Logic." I have not seen Zhou's translation. Judging from the name he has set, it should be "Small Logic," whether it is a complete translation is unknown. We have not yet seen a Chinese translation of Hegel's "Science of Logic" (that is, Great Logic).

Spring and Autumn

Six Bureaus

— Yan Qiao

In Suzhou, during weddings, funerals, and celebrations, there are so-called "Six Bureaus," which are indispensable servants, as these people are professionals who make a living from it. According to Wu Zimou's "Meng Liang Lu" of the Song Dynasty, under the article "Four Divisions and Six Bureaus for Banquets":

"The Fruit Bureau manages and arranges fruit platters, seasonal fruits, northern and southern fruits, preserved meats, sauces, and decorative fruit arrangements, and offers items for toasting. The Candied Fruit Bureau manages and arranges candied fruit platters, mountain-shaped candied fruits, and decorative arrangements. The Vegetable Bureau manages the platters on the banquet table, providing vegetables for the banquet, exotic vegetables, seasonal flavors, pickled vegetables, and decorative arrangements. The Oil and Candle Bureau manages lighting, upper candles, repairing candles, lighting lamps, arranging seats, holding bean lamps, bamboo lanterns, and arranging charcoal. The Incense and Medicine Bureau manages ambergris and borneol, peaceful and blessed fragrant incense, incense burners, incense balls, arranging incense and cleaning up ashes, listening for incense changes, and offering special sobering soups and pastries after drinking. The Arrangement Bureau manages chairs and tables, armchairs, desks, and sweeping, dusting, and cleaning. "

Today's Six Bureaus have undergone considerable changes. Fruits and candied fruits can be purchased from shops. Vegetables are supplied by restaurants. What the Oil and Candle Bureau and the Incense and Medicine Bureau manage largely belongs to tea vendors, and what the Arrangement Bureau manages belongs to sedan chair carriers. Therefore, although it is called Six Bureaus, it is no longer completely the old system. However, what exists now is often what did not exist in the past, such as music groups, cannons, and external servants (those belonging to the broker's license umbrella), etc. However, "Meng Liang Lu" also mentions the Four Divisions, one being the Account Setting Division, one being the Tea and Wine Division, one being the Kitchen Division, and one being the Table Setting Division, which are still commonly used today. It can be seen that the Four Divisions and Six Bureaus have been passed down for hundreds of years, some surviving, some abolished, some merged, and some combined, resulting in old names but not old systems. The people of the Six Bureaus are of mixed character, and they use all kinds of deceitful means, so if you are not an insider, you will suffer a great loss. Therefore, the accountant becomes the leader of the Six Bureaus, directing and developing for the host, which is in line with what "Meng Liang Lu" says: "The command bureau is divided, it can be gathered immediately, and all can be done according to the ritual." "Only those who are familiar with the work will not lose the festival, saving the host's labor."

In addition, there is also a special organization called Sedan Chair Heads, with designated areas and locations that do not encroach on each other. When a daughter is married and sends dowry, it must be done through these people. As a result, they arbitrarily demand prices, which is frightening. The valuation is mostly hosted by the matchmaker on behalf of the groom's family the day before the wedding. If the matchmaker is soft-spoken and kind-hearted and does not face the market, it is rare not to be ripped off. A friend of mine married a woman, and the estimated value of the dowry (referring to utensils) did not exceed three hundred gold, but the sedan chair heads received a reward of one hundred and twenty yuan. When Wang Yincai was the mayor, there was a proposal to abolish it, but in the end, it was decided that because these people's livelihoods depended on it, it was feared that they would become pests to society if they lost their jobs, so it was not implemented. However, it is ultimately a bad habit, and not abolishing it causes the bride's family to suffer greatly.

Officiating and Oath-Taking

— Yan Ye

A couple gets married in a magnificent hall, and in addition to relatives and friends coming to participate, they must also invite someone of higher status than the newlyweds to officiate the wedding, and give them words of encouragement, wishing them respect, love, and a long life together. It seems that this marriage must be officiated by the officiant to truly be able to grow old together. What ministers, directors, and committee members swear to take office in solemn halls, also in addition to the participation of colleagues, subordinates, and guests, must be supervised by superiors from their higher-level agencies or send personnel to the scene to supervise the oath, and also give them words of encouragement. It also seems that the oath of office taker to the Premier in heaven must be heard by the supervisor in order to prove and guarantee that they will be able to implement it in the future.

In fact, there are iron-like facts everywhere and at all times to prove that the effectiveness of this officiating and oath-taking has also encountered failure. Officiating is a product of modern marriage, and divorce news has occupied large spaces in newspapers in recent years. Divorce cases are a major business for lawyers and a complicated matter for judges. These many divorced people all invited officiants when they got married, and even the officiant's blessings are still in their ears but they have divorced. What is the effect of officiating? Oath-taking is also a product of the new era. Generally, rebels and traitors, as well as corrupt officials, swear an oath that is so pleasing to the ear when they take office under the supervision of the oath-taker. They accept the oath-taker's words of encouragement more sincerely. However, with the oath-taker's words of encouragement still in their ears, and the oath taken in the oath-taker's ears, they act recklessly. What is the effect of oath-taking?

After officiating a wedding, the officiant considers it a completed task and does not ask about anything else. After supervising an oath, the supervisor considers it a completed task and does not ask about anything else. Officiating and oath-taking are only solemn formalities for weddings and oaths and do not actually contribute to anything later, so I would like to propose here to cancel the officiating thing? What should be done with oath-taking? It concerns the party and the country, so I dare not speak nonsense.

The Story of Master Cha San

— Li Anfu

Master Cha San, whose name was Xiaoshan, was one of the wealthiest people in the late Qing Dynasty. At the same time, Master Sha San of Wumen was also a wealthy man. One day, Master Cha San traveled to Wumen and invited Master Sha San to drink. The food at the banquet was so abundant that it was incomparable. Later, Master Sha San wanted to do his best as a host and return the invitation to Master Cha San. But after thinking about it, he lacked a few famous chefs, so he sent someone to Master Cha San to ask for help. Cha sent fifty chefs to Sha's house to prepare the banquet for him. The doorman of Sha's house saw so many chefs and felt very strange. He hurried in to inform the host. The host personally walked into the kitchen and saw that those in charge of roasting ducks, roasting pigs, making snacks, and washing vegetables and fruits already occupied forty-six people. And only four people were in charge of cooking. Master Sha San thought to himself that his kitchen was too small. Not only were the chefs very inconvenient, but his own face was not very dignified. So he spent three days hiring dozens of craftsmen to enlarge the kitchen. Then he prepared a banquet, sent out invitations, and invited Master Cha San. After Master Cha San arrived, Master Sha San humbly said, "It was prepared in a hurry, I'm afraid it won't suit your taste." Master Cha San listened and smiled, saying:

"In the past, every time I went out, I always brought one hundred and twenty chefs. Later, it happened that the Holy Emperor made a southern tour, so I reduced it by forty people. Now I only have eighty people with me! When I arrived here, I was asked to borrow some, so I only sent fifty people, except for thirty people for my own use. Really! The number of people is small, and the time is short. I'm afraid it won't be as you, the host, intended!" After saying that, they laughed together.

Another time, Master Cha San walked into an antique shop. As soon as he stepped into the doorway, he suddenly heard the myna in the cage hanging on the eaves shouting: "Master Cha San is here! Master Cha San is here!" Master Cha San felt very happy in his heart. A few days later, Master Cha San went to the shop again, and the myna shouted again. Master Cha San really liked it in his heart, so he asked the shopkeeper how much he wanted to sell it for. The shopkeeper pretended to be alarmed and said: "This myna is寄托 from a friend and is not from this shop." Otherwise, I will give it to you as a gift. Why do you need to ask about selling it or not?" Master Cha San called the shopkeeper to ask his friend how much he wanted to sell it for. The shopkeeper went for a long time and came back and said, "My friend is unwilling to sell it." Master Cha San ordered him to discuss it with his friend again, but he was still unwilling. Master Cha San was angry and said: "No matter how much money this myna wants to sell for, I am willing to pay." So the shopkeeper pretended to go one more time and then said, "It won't sell for less than one hundred taels of silver." After hearing this, Master Cha San threw down one hundred taels of silver and walked away with the myna.

Master Cha San carried the myna home with a happy mood. Who knew that after a few days, he realized that the myna he bought for one hundred taels of silver could only shout "Master Cha San is here!" It couldn't say a single other word. After the fact, Master Cha San realized that he had been deceived by the shopkeeper.
