Talking About Vacuum

— Cheng Fanqun

There are many types of vacuum tubes. Any sealed glass tube with several electrodes inside, and with the air inside pumped out to a very low pressure, or replaced with other gases at extremely low pressure, such as X-ray tubes, mercury arc lamps, rectifier tubes, photoelectric tubes, Geissler Tubes, and radio vacuum tubes, are collectively referred to as vacuum tubes.

Is there nothing but electrodes inside the vacuum tube? In reality, even if the pressure inside the tube is reduced to one-millionth of atmospheric pressure, there are still hundreds of trillions of gas molecules inside the tube.

Before explaining the physical concept of vacuum, let's first talk about the structure of gases. At 20 degrees Celsius and 760 mmHg atmospheric pressure, every cubic centimeter of gas contains approximately 2.52 x 10^19 molecules. Now, let's take hydrogen as an example to illustrate the spatial occupancy of hydrogen atoms under the above conditions. Because the diameter of a hydrogen atom is approximately 10^-8 cm, the actual volume occupied by hydrogen is only one-millionth of a cubic centimeter. Although this value is not very precise, it can be generally said that even under atmospheric pressure, there are many gaps between gas molecules. If the pressure on the gas decreases, then the gaps between molecules increase even more. The usual meaning of vacuum refers to the pressure of the gas in a sealed container being reduced to a minimum!

Suppose the gas pressure inside the tube is reduced to one-millionth of atmospheric pressure, such a vacuum can be said to be very high, because this pressure is equivalent to 0.00076 mmHg or 0.0987 "bar" (see note for the definition of "bar"). At this time, the actual volume occupied by hydrogen gas is approximately one-millionth of one-millionth of the space. Therefore, from this point of view, such a degree of vacuum is indeed extremely high.

However, on the other hand, any gas under this 0.987 "bar" pressure still has 2.52 x 10^13 molecules per cubic centimeter, or 2.52 x 10^10 molecules per cubic millimeter. Therefore, the space is still filled with gas molecules.

In fact, radio vacuum tubes utilize the phenomenon of thermionic emission, and should be called thermionic tubes to be more accurate. (See pages 43 and 44 of "Radio Reader" by Huang Jiancai)

Note: One "bar" is the pressure of one dyne per square centimeter, and one "bar" is equivalent to 1.0133 x 10^-6 atmospheric pressure.

Triple Twin Tube

— Wang Mengcheng

A vacuum tube containing two triodes in one bulb is called a Triple Twin Tube. There are a total of seven electrodes inside the tube, as shown in the attached diagram. The triode on the left is connected to the input circuit and is called the input section; the triode on the right is connected to the output circuit and is called the output section. The two filaments are connected in parallel inside the tube, and a single A battery is used to supply the filament current. However, the filament of the input section indirectly provides heat, causing the cathode to heat up and emit electrons. This cathode is directly connected to the grid of the output section inside the vacuum tube. The output section does not have a cathode; electrons are emitted directly from the filament.

American-made triple twin tubes include the 295 AC tube, the 291 DC tube, and several types used in automobile radios, such as the 293 model. According to experiments, compared to pentodes, this type of triple twin tube can achieve twice the audio power output with the same plate voltage, and the sensitivity is increased by more than three times. The effectiveness is thus evident.

The maximum value of the input voltage applied to the power amplifier tube is usually limited by the negative voltage connected in the grid circuit. Beyond this limit, the total impedance of the grid circuit decreases, and grid current occurs. When the IP-Eg characteristic curve reaches the positive grid voltage section, the plate output becomes distorted. However, with the triple twin tube, both the positive and negative grid voltage sections of the IP-Eg characteristic curve can be utilized. The total impedance of the grid circuit remains extremely high, and the distortion of the plate output is minimal. Therefore, it can minimize distortion and maximize output under the same load.

Among various multiple frequencies connected to the triple twin tube, the distortion of the second frequency is the most significant. The distortion of the third frequency and above is very small and difficult to detect. If the triple twin tube is connected in a push-pull circuit and used, the distortion of the second frequency can be completely eliminated. In public places and movie theaters, it is most important to have a very large and undistorted audio power output. Using triple twin tubes can not only eliminate many stages of audio amplification, but also produce a natural sound quality with minimal distortion.

Manufacturing Vacuum Tubes

— Wei Xin Su

The dimensions of the various components inside a vacuum tube must be extremely precise, and the materials must be extremely pure. The measurements used often need to be calculated down to a few thousandths of an inch. For example, the weight of the emission coating applied to the filament is as small as 21 millionths of a pound. All of these components must undergo precise measurements through chemical testing before they can be used.

After the components are prepared, the next step is to manufacture the glass core. A standard length of glass tube is continuously moved by a machine into a gradually increasing gas flame. When the lower end of the glass tube becomes soft like molten wax, a rotating conical mold is used to shape the edge into a喇叭shape, and then another flame is used to cut off the unnecessary portion. The lead wires and supports of each electrode are then inserted into this core, heated to a high temperature, and pressed tightly in a metal mold to fuse them together. Before the temperature of this core cools down, compressed air is blown into the pumping tube to create a hole for pumping air.

After precise inspection, the next step is to assemble the other components such as the plate, grid, filament, cathode, screen grid, and suppressor grid. These components are assembled and soldered by automatic machines, and the speed is truly dazzling to behold. In addition to the above components, there is also a small cup containing magnesium particles, which is finally connected to the grid support.

After the components are assembled and re-inspected, they are sent to the sealing machine. After the glass envelope of the vacuum tube is joined to the core in the flame, it is connected to a vacuum pump to remove the air. During the pumping process, the major metal parts are simultaneously subjected to strong heating by a powerful high-frequency current, so that the gases contained in the glass and metal objects in the vacuum tube can also be removed. When the pumping is about to be completed, the magnesium particles are caused to explode or turn into smoke. This smoke can absorb the remaining harmful gases and condense into a silver film on the inside of the glass envelope to maintain the life of the vacuum. After the pumping is completed, the vacuum tube is automatically sealed.

Then, the lead wires of each electrode of the vacuum tube are inserted into each pin. The glue that adheres the vacuum tube to the tube base and the metal cap on the top of the tube is dried in a baking oven. The lead wires exposed outside the pins are cut off and soldered with solder. Thus, the vacuum tube is completed.

Quick Method for Determining Vacuum Tube Characteristics

Although there are many characteristics of vacuum tubes, only the following three are commonly used:

1. Amplification Factor: The ratio of the plate voltage (Ep) to the grid voltage (Eg) required to change an equal amount of plate current is called the amplification factor of the vacuum tube. That is, the amplification factor U equals ΔEp/ΔEg.

2. Plate Resistance: The ratio of the change in a small amount of plate voltage (Ep) to the resulting change in plate current (Ip) is the plate resistance of the vacuum tube. In other words, the plate resistance Rp equals ΔEp/ΔIp. The unit is ohms. (The commonly referred to plate resistance is the plate AC resistance. DC resistance is not commonly used.)

3. Mutual Conductance: Mutual conductance is the ratio of the change in grid voltage (Eg) to the change in plate current (Ip). That is, mutual conductance Im equals ΔIp/ΔEg. The unit is Mho. The practical unit is micromho.

There are certainly many methods for finding the characteristics of vacuum tubes, but most of them rely on sophisticated instruments and complex formulas. The method introduced in this article is based on the above definitions and is intended for personal experimentation by general amateurs. It does not require precise instruments or complicated formulas.

As shown in the diagram, T is an OIA vacuum tube. First, adjust the filament voltage to the specified value of 5V. Assume that when the plate voltage is 135V and the grid voltage is 9V, the plate current is 3ma. Next, reduce the grid voltage to 6V (the plate voltage and filament voltage remain unchanged). Suppose that the plate voltage increases to 6ma at this time. Then return the grid voltage to the original value (still 9V). Increase the plate voltage until the plate current reaches 6ma. Suppose that the plate voltage at this time is 160V. According to the definition in the first item above, we get:

Next, find the plate resistance. Using the same method as above, assume that the grid voltage is 9V.

When the plate voltage is 135V, the plate current is 3m2o. Now, increase the plate voltage to 140V. If the plate current increases to 35ma, then according to the definition in the second item above, we get:

That is, the resistance of a oIA vacuum tube is 10,000 ohms at a plate voltage of 135-140V and a grid voltage of 9V.

(Note: The so-called plate resistance must be accompanied by a description of the conditions under which the vacuum tube was measured. It is meaningless to simply say that the plate resistance is 10,000 ohms.)

Finally, find the mutual conductance. Still using the same method as above, assume that when the plate voltage is 135V and the grid voltage is 9V, the plate current is 3mao. When the grid voltage is reduced to 7.5V, and the plate current increases to 4.2ma, then according to the definition in the third item above, we get:

When speaking of mutual conductance, it is also necessary to include a description of the conditions under which the vacuum tube was tested, because it varies with the plate resistance and plate current. As mentioned above, the mutual conductance of a —oIA vacuum tube is 800 micromhos at a plate voltage of 135V and a grid voltage of 9V.—7V.

Similarities and Differences Between AC and DC Tubes

— Shi Huayu

Vacuum tubes can be divided into two types, AC tubes and DC tubes, depending on the power source of the filament. However, there is no difference in their functions of detection, amplification, amplitude modulation, and oscillation. Vacuum tubes that use storage batteries or dry batteries to heat the filament are collectively referred to as DC vacuum tubes. Due to the inconvenience of carrying and charging batteries, people then thought about using AC power. However, although DC tubes have a center resistor after applying AC power, the AC noise cannot be completely avoided, so specially designed AC tubes were created. AC tubes usually use low-voltage filaments. Nowadays, there are also AC voltages of several tens of volts. However, most of them are 2.5 volts. DC tubes are 1, 1.2, 3, 3.5, and 6.3 volts, etc. However, due to the inconvenience of supplying filament power, the trend is always to use power-saving types. The current for heating the filament is not large, so the filament is mostly coated with oxide, which can save a lot of power compared to those coated with thorium under the same electron evaporation rate. The opposite is true for AC tubes; the filament current is often above one ampere. Some vacuum tubes, such as 71 and 10, can also be used for AC power because they take longer to heat the filament to a temperature sufficient to emit electrons. When these AC/DC vacuum tubes use AC power to heat the filament, their grid bias is often slightly higher than when using DC power. To avoid AC hum, AC tubes are often manufactured with indirect heating. The so-called indirect heating means that the heating element does not simultaneously emit electrons. The heating element is the filament that is energized, but it is not directly related to the radio circuit. Its periphery is a porcelain tube. When the filament passes current and generates heat, the heat is transferred to the porcelain tube, and then from the porcelain tube to the metal cylindrical plate attached to the outside of the porcelain tube. This metal plate indirectly receives the heat from the filament and then evaporates electrons. The plate of an AC tube also sometimes uses a metal mesh made of tungsten, such as the 27 types. Vacuum tubes that use AC power to heat the filament have a longer lifespan than those using DC power because their filament temperature is more even. The load of AC tubes is also larger than that of DC tubes. The other parts are the same for both types, but AC tubes can be heated with DC power, although they consume more power. However, DC tubes are not suitable for heating with AC power because AC hum is unavoidable.

The World's Oldest Vacuum Tube

— RF

Fifty years ago, the world's inventor genius Thomas Edison discovered that when the filament of an electric light bulb is incandescent, if a small metal screen is placed next to it, there will be a current flowing between the filament and the screen. This phenomenon is the basis of the currently used vacuum tube. At that time, Edison specially made several such light bulbs with an extra small metal piece for further experimentation. Carbonized bamboo silk was used as the filament, and a section of thin metal wire was erected on both sides of the filament as a small screen; the filament and the screen were sealed together in a glass bulb evacuated to a vacuum. This special electric light bulb can be said to be the world's oldest vacuum tube.

Last year, the National Broadcasting Company (NBC) specially took this special light bulb made by Edison on that day and assembled it into a radio receiver. Its circuit is as shown in the figure, and it uses 110 volts of DC power to heat the filament. After it was made, it was used to receive the broadcast from radio station WJZ, and the sound it received was input to radio station WEAF, which then rebroadcast it for people to listen to. According to listeners at that time: "The sound rebroadcast in this way is still very beautiful and comparable to the original broadcast of radio station WEAF."

In this case, the invention of the diode vacuum tube did not begin in 1904, nor was it invented by Fleming; but its invention actually dates back to fifty years ago, and its inventor was actually the genius Edison. It's just that Edison didn't know at that time that this special electric light bulb had this special function.

Revival and Use of Discarded Vacuum Tubes

— KMK

Burning out a vacuum tube is indeed the most disappointing thing for amateur researchers. If the filament is not broken, but the efficiency of electron emission is lost, or if the distance between the breaks in the filament is not far, there may still be a glimmer of hope. Various methods can be used to revive it. This method of revival has already been introduced in this magazine and does not need to be repeated.

If the broken filament is no longer in its original position, or if the distance between the breaks is too far, and it cannot be revived by the above method, then is it not a discarded vacuum tube? Now I will introduce a simple revival method to revive discarded vacuum tubes, so that researchers can recover a lot of their economic losses!

First, connect the vacuum tube with the broken filament as shown in (Figure 1). Gently tap the outside of the vacuum tube with your finger a few times until you hear a "click" sound in the earpiece. At this time, the broken filament is already connected to the grid circuit (G)! Then connect it to a dry battery as shown in (Figure 2) to see if the filament is bright. Then, burn the outer circumference of the vacuum tube with an alcohol lamp until the glass turns slightly red. After it cools down, the broken filament has fused with the grid circuit (G). Use it as a (diode) rectifier tube with the connection method shown in (Figure 3). Its efficiency and work are no different from a diode vacuum tube. The only difference is that the filament voltage (FF) is slightly smaller.

Members of Your House Will Question the Minister of Education

(China United Press, Tokyo, 23rd) The Far Eastern Games will be held in Little Luzon this summer. Japan has been promoting the participation of the puppet state of Manchukuo in the games. Because of our opposition, its intention has not been fulfilled. The Japanese side negotiated with us, but we have repeatedly refused. Although it has induced the Philippines and other participating countries to support its claims, it has still not obtained their support, so there is no way to resolve the matter. Recently, it has aroused the attention of the Japanese political circles. It is said that the problem will be politicized.

He is scheduled to return to the United States on May 25th. He will go to Japan in early October. Strangely, England is not on his itinerary.

Australia's Hope for the Davis Cup is Not High (Sydney Reuters) According to Malcolm, secretary of the Australian Lawn Tennis Association and a member of the Davis Cup selection committee, Australia's hope of winning the Davis Cup today is no stronger than last year, and not as hopeful as most people think. This is because Japanese players are improving very quickly, and they are becoming more balanced. The United States is also a difficult team to beat. In the current situation, it seems that everything will depend on Crawford alone. In order to make Crawford devote all his efforts to singles, Hopman and Quist have been tested in cooperation, and the results are very good. According to his opinion, Quist is even more hopeful than Crawford.

The Old Gentlemen Qingbai Game Did Not End in the Slanting Rain

But Seeing People Fall and Prostrate Themselves

Yesterday was the scheduled meeting date for the Wangping Street Old Gentlemen Soldiers and the Hankou Qingbai team at the baseball field. Although the weather was very good, the punctual and trustworthy Old Gentlemen arrived at the venue at 3:30 p.m. to attend a military conference. The Old Gentlemen who had wives also brought their beautiful spouses and lively children to support them. No one was willing to be a straggler under the mobilization order. This shows the undiminished ambition of the Old Gentlemen in their twilight years. After the Old Gentlemen Soldiers held a military conference and discussed their offensive and defensive plans, they braved the rain to test their feet and waited quietly for the enemy to come and challenge them. At 3:40, the light rain, although getting heavier and heavier, did not stop Director Pan Gongzhan and Mr. Shen Huichun from arriving one after another. One was prepared to throw the ball, and the other was prepared to enforce the law, but because it was still early, they could only watch from the sidelines.

Later, the clock struck four, and the Old Gentlemen Soldiers were ready, but not a single soldier from the Hankou Qingbai team arrived. Everyone knew that the Qingbai team had probably forgotten the agreed time. So, they divided into two armies, briefly practiced, and exercised.

The Old Gentlemen Soldiers were practicing enthusiastically when suddenly it was reported that the enemy was approaching. Everyone looked intently and saw that the Qingbai team had arrived late. Although it was already 4:30 at this time, more than 30 minutes past the competition time, it didn't seem to be a problem in the eyes of people who didn't value time and couldn't keep their word. But since the Qingbai team had arrived, but their troops were incomplete, they had to borrow soldiers from the Old Gentlemen team. So, the Old Gentlemen team, with their abundance of talent, lent four generals to Qingbai, and they began to line up for battle.

At this time, the slanting wind and fine rain surrounded the baseball field. The two armies exchanged artillery fire under Director Pan Gongzhan's wind-assisted ball throw and Mr. Shen Huichun's rain-soaked law enforcement. Unfortunately, not long after the hand-to-hand combat began, the wind and rain grew stronger, and the ground was muddy, making it unsuitable for running. One person fell prostrate on the ground, while another fell face up. Under the circumstances of people falling and horses stumbling, they completely lost their combat effectiveness. The impartial referee, seeing this situation, sounded the gong to call off the battle. The friendly competition ended with no winner or loser on either side.

Second Day of the Jiangsu Provincial Local Education Inspection Conference

▲Held Sub-area Meetings in the Morning, Held the Second General Meeting in the Afternoon

▲Six Normal School Areas Exchange Inspections, Departing on March 5th

(Zhenjiang, 23rd) The Jiangsu Provincial Local Inspection Conference was held at the Education Department at 9 a.m. yesterday (the 23rd). Sub-area meetings were held, with the six normal school areas as units, and the principals of the normal schools in each normal school area were responsible for convening the meetings. The discussions were completed successively by 12 p.m. The main points of the discussion were the method of exchanging inspection names and the distribution plan for county superintendents within each area, as well as the departure date and inspection points. The second general meeting was held at 3 p.m. to discuss various cases. The closing ceremony will be held today. The situation of the sub-area meetings is listed below:

First Area: Zhenjiang, Jiangpu, Yangzhong, Yizheng, Ga淳, 溧水, Liuhe, Danyang, Jurong, Jiangdu, and other ten counties. Cao Chu, Principal of the Zhenjiang Normal School of the Province, Wang Zongjin, Elementary Education Instructor, and more than ten county superintendents attended. It was decided to exchange the names of the county superintendents for mutual inspection within the area. The list included Chen Deji of Zhenjiang, Zhu Shigui of Jiangpu, Yangzhong, and Yizheng, Wang Enrong of Ga淳 and 溧水, Chen Liangwu of Liuhe, Cao Naigao of Danyang, He Zhongning of Jurong, and Zhao Jinrun of Jiangdu.

Second Area: Wuxi, Yixing, Wujin, Jiangyin, Liyang, Jingjiang, Jint坛, Wuxian, Wujiang, Changshu, and other ten counties. Shen Peixian, Principal of Wuxi Normal School of the Province, Wu Hengtong, Xin Zengyao, Elementary Education Instructors, and county superintendents attended. It was decided to exchange the names of the superintendents for mutual inspection. The list included Hu Chaolun, Xu Zaofei, Xu Shaolie of Wuxi, Wei Shanglun, Zhao Shengchong of Yixing, Yang Binru, Huang Yue, Peng Shifang of Wujin, Deng Yongding, Xue Jinshan of Jiangyin, Yuan Xianzhang of Liyang, Meng Yuqi of Jingjiang, Huang Zhili of Jint坛, Song Miao, Wang Shiheng, Shen Xianzhi of Wuxian, Xu Wenlan of Wujiang, Sun Youguang, Ding Qipeng of Changshu.

Third Area: Taicang, Kunshan, Jiading, Shanghai, Songjiang, Baoshan, Nanhui, Qingpu, Fengxian, Jinshan, Chuansha, Chongming, and other twelve counties. Zheng Mian, Principal of Taicang Normal School, Xu Shoukang, Instructor, and more than ten county superintendents attended. Zheng Mian presided over the meeting. It was decided to exchange the names of the superintendents for mutual inspection. The list included Wang Zhengbing of Taicang, Zhang Jingxin of Kunshan, Xiao Chonggan of Jiading, Wei Guangjiong and He Huanzhang of Shanghai and Songjiang jointly inspected, Shen Baoyu of Baoshan, Wan Yongkang and Xu Jie of Nanhui, Zhang Zicheng of Qingpu, Wang Zhizuo of Fengxian, Chen Zhijun of Jinshan, Zhu Changlin and Shen Ji of Chuansha and Chongming.

Fourth Area: Huaiyin, Funing, Siyang, Suqian, Lianshui, Muyang, Gaoyou, Baoying, Huai'an, and other nine counties. Gu Kebin, Principal of Huai Normal School of the Province, and instructors and superintendents attended. It was decided to exchange the names of the superintendents for mutual inspection as follows: Bao Dehua of Huaiyin and Funing, Qian Zhengcai, Ge Yinghua and Tian Qichang of Siyang and Suqian, Xu Tigong and Liu Zhanke of Lianshui and Muyang, Shi Ying of Gaoyou, and Li Bingzi and Zhu Ruitong of Huai'an.

Fifth Area: Donghai, Guanyun, Fengpei, Xiaoxiao, Pixian, Ganyu, Tongshan, Suining, and other counties. Cao Zhongquan, Principal of Donghai Normal School, Jiang Xipeng, Wang Mingyu, Instructors, and county superintendents attended. It was decided to exchange the names of the superintendents for mutual inspection as follows: Wang Ruhong of Donghai and Guanyun, Yan Zhensheng of Fengxian, Guan Xiangxun of Xiaoxian, Wang Changyu of Pixian and Ganyu, Ma Lixun of Tongshan, Feng Yukun of Peixian, Wei Shizhang of Xiaoshan, and Chen Baotai of Suining.

Sixth Area: Rugao, Taixing, Taixian, Qidong, Nantong, Dongtai, Yancheng, Xinghua, Haimen, and other nine counties. Xu Xun, Principal of Rugao Normal School, and instructors and superintendents attended. It was decided to exchange the names of the superintendents for mutual inspection as follows: Yao Gen, Song Zhaohang of Rugao, Wu Puyun of Taixing, Wang Lianzhen of Taixian, Xi Yunpeng of Qidong, Yu Weizhao, Zhao Mingcheng of Nantong, Pan Dejun, Zhai Yigu, Liu Xuexiu of Dongtai and Yancheng, Liu Zongxun of Xinghua, and Sun Zheng of Haimen. (Note) After the superintendent of Funing County submits his report to the department, he will join the inspection of Yancheng.

Measures for County Superintendents to Exchange Inspections The Jiangsu Provincial Local Education Inspection Conference held its first general meeting at 2 p.m. on the 23rd, and passed measures such as the exchange of inspections by county superintendents. The original text is as follows: Article 1. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has formulated these measures to improve inspection efficiency and improve local education. Article 2. The exchange of inspections by county superintendents shall, for the time being, be based on the same normal school area as the principle. Article 3. The exchange of inspections shall be based on the county as a unit. In counties with a particularly large number of educational institutions, two or three people may be assigned to carry out the inspection. In counties with fewer educational institutions, one person may inspect two or three counties. Article 4. The number of educational institutions inspected by each superintendent within a semester shall, for the time being, be based on 100 schools and 300 classes as the principle. (Each private school is equivalent to one class.) Each school district must be inspected regularly. Article 5. When inspecting the educational institutions in each county, each superintendent shall, at any time, guide the inspection work of the education committee members or the principals of the central elementary schools in each district, and the directors of the central institutions in the public education area, and assess their performance. Article 6. The inspection points and inspection forms shall be formulated and promulgated by the Department of Education. Article 7. After completing the inspection, each superintendent shall, in addition to submitting a plan for improvement to the principal of the normal school in each normal school area, prepare a detailed report within three weeks and submit it to the department for verification and handling. Article 8. If each superintendent finds a school or educator during the inspection and has the following circumstances, he/she may implement emergency treatment and prepare a temporary report to be submitted to the department for verification and handling: A. The number of students is too small, and the class must be stopped or merged. B. Teachers and staff arbitrarily absent from their duties. C. Unethical conduct that tarnishes their character. D. Imprudent integrity that encroaches on public funds. E. Reactionary thoughts that have been verified with evidence. Article 9. The travel expense standards and payment procedures for each superintendent's inspection shall be determined separately. Article 10. Before and after each superintendent exchanges inspections, a sub-area meeting shall be held once, which shall be convened regularly by the principal of the provincial normal school in the normal school area. Article 11. The detailed rules for the implementation of the exchange inspection shall be formulated separately by the sub-area meeting in light of the circumstances of each area. Article 12. The implementation of the exchange inspection shall be guided by the principal of the provincial normal school in each normal school area. Article 13. These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education and submitted to the provincial government for record.

Matters that should be noted by the elementary education instructors, county superintendents, central elementary school principals, and county education committees during the period when county superintendents exchange inspections: 1. Elementary education instructors and county superintendents should attend the sub-area inspection meeting. 2. When the elementary education instructor inspects the elementary education in each county, the county superintendent, the principal of the central school, and the education committee members of each district should report the general situation of county education and the main points for improvement at any time. 3. If the instructor has any questions regarding the inspection, the county superintendent, the principal of the central school, and the education committee members of each district should answer them truthfully. 4. The county superintendent may consult with the instructor to pay special attention to the guidance of schools or teachers who are considered to need special guidance. 5. The instructor and the county superintendent, the principal of the central school, and the education committee members should exchange opinions on the inspection and may hold a county inspection meeting. 6. Regarding the improvement of county education and teacher training, the instructor and the county superintendent, the principal of the central school, and the education committee members should discuss the methods with each other.

The Second General Meeting Yesterday The Jiangsu Provincial Local Education Inspection Conference held its second general meeting yesterday afternoon, the 23rd. The main items decided were: 1. Detailed rules for the implementation of the exchange inspection; 2. Methods for the distribution of each superintendent's inspection work; 3. The inspection will begin on March 5th and end at the end of June; 4. Request the department to stipulate the forms for civil schools and the main points for the improvement of private schools passed by the inspection review committee.

Revised Regulations for Overseas Chinese Primary and Secondary Schools by the Ministry of Education

The Ministry of Education recently revised the regulations for overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools as follows: Chapter I, General Principles: Article 1: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall abide by the educational aims of the Republic of China and the principles of general education in its implementation policies, based on the special environment of overseas Chinese, and in accordance with the physical and mental development of students, cultivate national consciousness, self-governing organizational skills, and knowledge and skills for improving life and developing production. Article 2: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall, in principle, be established and operated by the local overseas Chinese through fundraising. Article 3: The establishment of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall follow the current national education system. The primary school study period is six years, with the first four years being elementary primary school and the last two years being advanced primary school. Elementary primary schools may be established independently. The secondary school study period is three years for junior high school and three years for senior high school, both of which may be established independently. The aforementioned study period may be flexibly handled with the approval of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission in consultation with the Ministry of Education, depending on the special circumstances of the locality. Article 4: Overseas Chinese primary schools may be affiliated with kindergartens. Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools may be affiliated with supplementary schools and other social education institutions. Article 5: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall apply for registration in accordance with the provisions of Article 1 of the revised regulations for the registration of overseas Chinese schools. Article 6: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be subject to the supervision and guidance of the consular officer in charge or personnel dispatched by the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission to investigate or manage overseas Chinese education. Chapter II, Funding: Article 7: The funding of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be collected by the founders in accordance with local conditions using the following methods: (1) Surtax on overseas Chinese business tax; (2) Import and export local product tax or department store tax; (3) Overseas Chinese special business tax; (4) Monthly, annual, or special donations from overseas Chinese organizations, shops, or individuals; (5) Other donations. Article 8: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools may receive subsidies from the national government. Article 9: The financial affairs of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be made public. The accounting methods and management methods of school property shall be formulated by the school board and three copies shall be prepared, one of which shall be submitted to the consular office in charge for record, and the remaining two copies shall be submitted to the consular office in charge to be forwarded to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and the Ministry of Education. Article 10: Items such as the allocation of funds for overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be based on the standards set by the Ministry of Education, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, or the consular office in charge, if any. Chapter III, Facilities: Article 11: The address of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be chosen in a place that does not hinder hygiene and morality and is convenient for teaching. Article 12: The school buildings, sports grounds, and all facilities of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools must be suitable for the principles of education and hygiene. Article 13: The construction and equipment of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be based on the standards and methods set by the Ministry of Education or the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, if any. However, due to local circumstances, the standards and methods set by the local government for general primary and secondary schools may also be adopted. Chapter IV, Curriculum: Article 14: The curriculum of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be implemented in accordance with the curriculum standards for primary and secondary schools formulated by the Ministry of Education, but due to special local circumstances, it may be submitted to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission for consultation with the Ministry of Education for modification. Article 15: Textbooks for overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be selected by the primary and secondary school textbook compilation committee organized by the consular officer in charge or personnel dispatched by the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission to handle overseas Chinese education, together with local overseas Chinese education groups and representatives of overseas Chinese primary and secondary school teachers and staff, from the textbooks approved by the Ministry of Education, and schools may choose to adopt several types for the sake of adapting to local conditions, and the committee may also modify or re-edit them. The overseas Chinese school-specific textbooks modified or re-edited in the preceding paragraph shall be submitted to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission for consultation and reviewed and approved by the Ministry of Education. Article 16: When overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools adopt foreign textbooks, the primary and secondary school textbook compilation committee shall select or review the teaching materials and make distinctions. Article 17: Except for foreign languages, overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall use Mandarin Chinese as the language of instruction. Primary schools shall not use classical Chinese textbooks. Article 18: The academic affairs of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be based on the standards and methods set by the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, if any. Chapter V, Moral Education: Article 19: The management of students in overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be treated equally, and corporal punishment shall not be implemented. Article 20: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall take the common life of teachers and students as the principle, and all regulations shall be jointly observed. Article 21: The moral education of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be the joint responsibility of all teachers and staff. All teachers and staff shall adopt a cooperative and consistent attitude in guiding students' self-study and self-government, assessing students' character and behavior, and connecting families to serve the society. Article 22: The moral education of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be based on the standards and methods set by the Ministry of Education or the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, if any. Chapter VI, School Board: Article 23: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall establish a school board, and its functions are as follows: (1) Fundraising and safekeeping of funds; (2) Purchasing and safekeeping of school property; (3) Planning annual expenses and temporary expenses for construction and equipment; (4) Selecting and re-appointing the principal; (5) Reviewing budgets and final accounts; (6) Handling school property registration matters; (7) Representing the school in handling negotiations with the local government. The organizational regulations of the school board of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be formulated separately. Article 24: When school board members of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools have suggestions for the development of school affairs, they shall be submitted to the school board meeting for discussion and resolution, and then handed over to the principal for appropriate handling. Article 25: If, due to special local circumstances, overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools cannot establish a school board, the founders of the school may submit a request to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission in consultation with the Ministry of Education for exemption from establishing the functions of the school board listed in Article 23 of these regulations, which shall be exercised by the founders. Chapter VII, Teachers and Staff: Article 26: Each overseas Chinese primary and secondary school shall have one principal, who shall be full-time. However, elementary primary schools with fewer grades may be concurrently held by a full-time teacher of the school. Article 27: The functions of the principal of an overseas Chinese primary and secondary school are as follows: (1) Presiding over all school affairs; (2) Appointing teachers and staff; (3) Preparing budgets and final accounts. Article 28: The principal of an overseas Chinese primary and secondary school may attend school board meetings and may submit proposals, but has no voting rights. Article 29: The principal of an overseas Chinese primary and secondary school shall be qualified if he or she embraces the Three Principles of the People, has a sound personality, can live with students, and possesses one of the following qualifications: (1) Secondary school principal: (A) Graduated from a junior college or above, has a research background in education, and has held an educational position for more than one year; (B) Graduated from a junior college or above, whose specialty is consistent with the nature of the school, and has held an educational position for more than one year; (C) Has made special contributions to secondary school education or a certain academic field, which can be proven by achievements, and has held an educational position for more than five years; (2) Primary school principal: (A) Graduated from a normal school or above with a level equivalent to high school; (B) Graduated from a senior high school or above with research in education; (C) Graduated from an old-system secondary school and has served as a primary school teacher for more than two years; (D) Has made special contributions to primary school education, which can be proven by achievements, and has served as a primary school teacher for more than three years. Article 30: Teachers of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall, in principle, be full-time. In addition to teaching, they shall also be assigned to all other school affairs of the school. Article 31: Teachers of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be qualified if they embrace the Three Principles of the People, have good moral character (such as no bad habits, etc.), have corresponding academic ability (such as Mandarin Chinese teachers must be fluent in Mandarin Chinese, etc.), and possess one of the following qualifications: (1) Secondary school teacher: (A) Graduated from a junior college or above, whose specialty is consistent with the subject taught; (B) Has specialized research in a certain subject that can be proven by achievements; (2) Primary school teacher: (A) Graduated from a normal school for more than six years; (B) Graduated from a junior high school or above and has experience in teaching methods; (C) Has made special contributions to primary school education, which can be proven by achievements, and has served as a primary school teacher for more than two years. Article 32: Overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools may, depending on the complexity of affairs, appropriately establish staff members such as secretaries, accountants, and general affairs personnel. Article 33: The appointment of principals, teachers, and staff of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be made by appointment letter. During the term of appointment, neither party may terminate the contract midway unless there is a definite dereliction of duty or other unavoidable accidents. Article 34: The annual salary of principals and teachers of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be calculated for twelve months. Accommodation shall be provided by the school in principle. For those hired domestically, round-trip travel expenses shall be provided by the school. However, if they are dismissed and do not return to the country but continue to work locally or within 200 miles of the area, the round-trip travel expenses to the country may be recovered. Article 35: The minimum salary for full-time teachers in overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be equivalent to five to ten times the average monthly food expenses per person in the locality. Article 36: Annual salary increases, pensions, retirement funds, and children's education funds for teachers and staff of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be formulated separately by the consular officer in charge, together with local overseas Chinese education groups, with reference to the standards or methods set by the Ministry of Education. Article 37: The professional development of teachers and staff of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be handled in accordance with the regulations for the professional development of primary and secondary school teachers and staff set by the Ministry of Education.

Two Heads of Fujian Education and Construction, Zheng Zhenwen and Chen Ticheng, Come to Shanghai Together

To Pay Respects to Officials in the Capital Last Night for Consultations

Zheng Zhenwen, member of the Fujian Provincial Government and concurrently Director of the Department of Education, and Chen Ticheng, concurrently Director of the Department of Construction, arrived in Shanghai by the new Ningxing merchant ship from Fujian the day before yesterday. They went to the capital last night. It is reported that Zheng's trip was due to the problem of education funding in Fujian Province. Historically, the 110,000 yuan of funding was originally allocated from the salt surplus. After the establishment of the Fujian Provincial Government, all the salt surplus was transferred to the central government. When Zheng took office, the central government had agreed to subsidize the full amount of the aforementioned education funding. However, the Fujian Central Bank refused to allocate the funds because it had not received a payment order from the central government. Therefore, Zheng left Fujian for the capital to discuss the matter with the Ministry of Finance. Chen Ticheng's trip was due to the central government's order to complete the Fujian-Zhejiang highway within a time limit, and it was necessary to consult with the National Government. Therefore, the two went to the capital together and are expected to return to Shanghai and Fujian within three to five days.

Free Talk

Northern and Southern Literature and Others

— Gu Ming

Rich imagination is determined by the clear and vast sky, and the dark and deep night; this is the source of religion and literature. If it is an extremely materialistic nation, in wind and sand and hardship, there is not much religion or literature. Examining the origin of the world's great religions, all in what kind of region and natural environment, will be surprised by the greatness of many natural forces!

We have never heard of great literature in Xinjiang, but Tibet has produced world-famous writers. Ordinary folk songs may have literary value, but may not be comparable to Homer. It seems that literature should not be divided into north and south, but from a subjective point of view, there are boundaries that can be divided.

Recently, for the sake of southern literature and northern literature, the Beijing school and the Shanghai school, it was lively for a while. But whether it is Beijing or Shanghai, whether it is surprised or horrified, although it is a school, it is ultimately different from literature. Most of the writers currently writing are southerners, and in the history of literature, it may not be specifically labeled "Beijing Literature". However, after many miscellaneous people flowed to that side, gradually moved into high-rise buildings, relied on the powerful, and there were no competitors in front, they naturally wanted to feel extraordinary and become such a school. Shanghai is the land of foreign slaves, compradors, and hooligans, a place to hide dirt and harbor filth, not a literary environment, which Beijing scholars do not need to know. But if there is literature, it will never be called "Hooligan Literature". Either they are famous by relying on officials, or they are merchants to compete for profit. Both are ridiculed, and there is no need to argue about who is the "orthodox".

Therefore, the reason why there are more southern figures than in the north is nothing more than changes in the natural environment. In the distant past, culture moved south, and in recent times, European winds moved east. The northwest was originally a wealthy land, and Wu and Yue were tribes with cut hair and tattooed bodies. Because people used the power of the land without cultivation, the land gradually became barren and the people became poor. Once the forests were used up, the rivers also changed their courses, and fertile land became wasteland. For example, the fire wells in Sichuan, burning for hundreds or thousands of years, will also extinguish. So run to places where life is easy, so move south. The culture of the Yellow River basin has dried up. When it reaches the Yangtze River and the Pearl River, life will become more difficult and culture will decline, so it will end up going south to the sea. At that time, maybe it can be called the "Shanghai School", but then, there will be nothing left.

The South can be considered rich in products, with beautiful mountains and clear waters, so modern times can still produce talents who specialize in dreaming and specializing in ideals, even if they are singing about the wind and moon, it is still in the surplus of material life. If you still hope to have great literary geniuses in the future, please pay attention to the modern material environment.

The Home of the Malays

— Hei Ying

It was a cloudy day early on Sunday. After eating breakfast, the sun had not yet come out. I didn't know what to do at home, so I wanted to invite a few friends out for a stroll.

Five people were riding four bicycles. Little Ya Zhen was afraid that she wouldn't have enough strength to ride, so she asked me to take her; the road was flat, but by the time I got to the second bridge, I was already behind.

"Work harder, look how far they've run."

She said, patting my spine from behind.

Sweat, like mountain springs, streamed down from my hair, onto my forehead, onto the side of my nose, and onto my neck. I wanted to pull out a handkerchief to wipe it, but if I took my hand away, the car might fall into the ditch; if it was just me, the sweat wouldn't flow so much, and there wouldn't be any danger in taking my hand away for a while.

After crossing the bridge, the scenery on both sides changed. At first, there were many desolate tombs, and the weeds grew half a foot high. As we continued to run, it gradually became desolate, and the road had no asphalt; sand and pebbles crackled under the wheels. Some coconut trees stood there unevenly, and some children walked past carrying a large bunch of bananas. After passing through a field planted with tobacco leaves, we entered "Ganjiang".

They stopped in front of a Malay's house, arranged their bicycles, and stood there waiting for me. We were familiar with the owner of this house. He came to the city from time to time, and bought rice and cloth in Ya Zhen's shop. When he saw us coming, he was so happy that his two rows of white teeth were fully exposed. He shook my hand to show his warm welcome. Walking into the wooden house, a gust of wind blew in from the back door, and it felt much cooler; the host knew we were thirsty and asked his wife to bring two coconuts. After drinking the fresh and sweet coconut water, she also sent a basket of fruit.

The furnishings of the house were extremely simple. A bed, a table, and chairs were placed in the middle. There were no paintings or photos, nor were there wardrobes or anything like that. Two naked children stared with unfamiliar eyes. Ya Zhen gave them a "rambutan". The taste of this fruit is no different from lychees in Guangdong.

"Why don't you wear clothes?"

A friend asked.

"They don't want to wear them."

"Is it like this every day?"

"Yes, they sleep naked too."

Their sons are so strong, they don't get sick all year round. When it rains, at most they only need to wear a single shirt.

The life of the Malays is simple and primitive. We played there until noon, and the host's wife had already prepared the meal; white rice with chili and dried fish was used to treat the guests. We, who grew up in Malay lands, naturally ate very well, but a friend who had come from China not long ago was embarrassed: only he ate with a spoon, while we all grabbed the rice with our hands.

After playing for half a day, the sun sneaked out at some point. When we went back, my car was loaded with two big durians, which Ya Zhen gave to the friend in the back.

Heartfelt Condemnation

— Bingying

These past few days, I've become even easier to anger, and poor Li has become my punching bag. She just had a fight with me and stormed off in anger. At the moment she slammed the door shut, I really wanted to run after her and hold her back, embrace her waist with both arms, look at her with pleading eyes, and say to her in a gentle voice: "Sister Li, forgive me, I was just acting like a child. If you really want to go out, take me with you!" But for some reason, my feet were as if nailed to the ground, unable to move. Even my eyes seemed to be covered by a black cloth, not seeing the ground. I heard a loud slamming of the door downstairs - even louder than the one she slammed here just now. I knew she had left, carrying boundless grievances.

Tears flowed from my eyes like a fountain. I wondered why I've been so sentimental lately, crying at the slightest thing. Before, I couldn't easily shed tears unless I used chili peppers to stimulate them.

Sitting blankly, the light of the tears was as clear as crystal, as clean and beautiful as the icicles hanging from the treetops in winter. From this, I seemed to see Li's face filled with anger and sorrow, dragging her lonely shadow through the crossroads, weeping on the rocky mountain. She definitely doesn't want to come back. Alas! Who would want to come back and be subjected to my anger?

Hearing the "ding ding ding" of the bell, I knew the first hour of class was over. The last tear fell, and Mother Li came in. I quickly pretended to be very calm and leaned over the table to write.

My heart was being oppressed tighter and tighter, making it difficult even to breathe. I wanted to cry out loud, or immediately go to the crowded streets to find Li. Even if I couldn't find her, and had to return with disappointment and sorrow at dusk, at least I would have punished myself, taken the punishment myself... Yes, that's it. I'll look for her. And so, with heavy steps, I came downstairs, onto Zhongshan Road.

Men, women, children, old people, even every lamppost, every rickshaw parked by the side of the road, all passed under the sharp gaze of my eyes. But disappointingly, though I saw many wearing light gray cloth qipaos, I couldn't find Li's shadow.

I walked many places and still couldn't find her. I saw that the clock in the policeman's booth already read four thirty.

I don't know how, but I actually ran to the area of Xiamen Road and Kaiyuan Road. At this time, I still hadn't given up hope. I thought she must have gone back and seen the note I left on the table. She should be rushing over. If we could meet here, I would definitely open my arms and hug her, regardless of everything.

Several heavy trucks sped past, dust flying into my eyes, almost blinding me. Following my footsteps, inexplicably, I suddenly came to the seaside.

I can't find her! At this point, I seemed completely despondent. But strangely, my heart suddenly felt much lighter, as if a stone had been dropped from it. There was no longer the anxiety I had just felt, nor any sorrow. I just blankly jumped into a small sampan and drifted lightly to the center of the sea.

The seawater was emerald green, the clouds were blue. In the northeast corner of the sky, floated a few cotton-like, pure white clouds. The unorderly Western-style buildings, under the azure sky, seemed particularly pitiful and boring. Really, I compared these gray Western-style buildings to spirit houses burned for the dead to live in, as if the people living inside were all corpses. Isn't that so? Those who toil all day at the docks and on the streets, where would they find such houses to live in? Only those living corpses, full of food and with nothing to do, have tall buildings to live in.

Because the wind was not strong, there were only slight waves. The boatman rowed very slowly. I felt as comfortable as if I were sleeping in my childhood cradle. Carefully studying the sudden changes in my mood these past few days, it's because my tinnitus has worsened, and my lungs are acting up again. I dare not go to the hospital for a check-up, even though the doctor has repeatedly told me that I must go for a check-up and weigh myself once a week, no matter what. But I dare not go, because I'm afraid he'll nag and say things like rest, get some sun, eat nutritious food.

The boatman asked me where I wanted to go. I wanted to answer him with a poetic phrase: "Let it drift!" But I don't know how to say it in Xiamen dialect. Even if I did, he wouldn't understand. So I just moved my mouth to the left, and he changed direction.

Life is empty, full of suffering. At this moment, I more deeply understood the meaning of this. Although in arduous struggles you can better grasp the meaning of life, it eventually becomes like it is now, when there is nothing left, and the heart is filled with empty sorrow, the bitterness of life.

Gradually, my head became too heavy to lift, and my forehead ached as if being struck by an iron hammer. The warm sunlight made me dizzy. And so, the little boat carried me, drifting for an hour and a half, and returned to the streets where I couldn't find Li's shadow.

Li, I hope you have returned safely. I, who have been condemned by my heart, am now unwilling to see you!

Cormorants

— Bai Yan

The boat gently glided out onto Poyang Lake. After passing Longkou, what met the eye was countless fishing rafts.

The rafts were all woven from bamboo, narrow and long in shape, with the front end upturned. On top were placed a bamboo basket and a low stool. On a bamboo pole beside the raft, several cormorants stood perched.

The fisherman only needed to bend his waist forward and push with the pole in his hand, and the bamboo raft would move forward like an arrow, lightly drawing two lines of ripples on the water.

The fishing rafts were arranged in formations on the water's surface, advancing in single file, or in a V-formation.

When they reached a suitable stretch of river, the fisherman knew there were many fish hidden in the water. With a shout, everyone drove the cormorants into the water together.

The fishermen shouted "Lu! Lu!" in their mouths, and the cormorants responded to the fishermen's calls with "Jia! Jia!". They slowly spread out.

Some splashed and flew on the water, others leisurely wandered in the water. Green eyes, hooked beaks. Looking around. As soon as they caught sight of a fish shadow flashing in front of them, they immediately somersaulted into the water and chased after it. Any fish that encountered them were like rabbits meeting hunting dogs. Few could escape safely.

After the cormorant caught a fish, it would raise its head, hold the fish in its mouth, and happily swim close to its master's bamboo raft. Then the master would take the fish from its mouth and throw it into the bamboo basket, and immediately take another small fish to feed it.

After eating, it would happily cry "Jia! Jia!" again, paddle away, and resume its fishing work.

In this way, the best cormorants could catch dozens of catties of fish every day. When the weather was clear and the river water was clear and the bottom could be seen, we could sit on the bow of the boat, lean against the awning, and leisurely focus on the water, watching the cormorants chase the swimming fish. Witnessing the struggle of the weak for survival, one couldn't help but feel a little sad.

But even though the cormorants work so hard for their masters, they rarely get to eat their fill.

Some say: It's not that the master doesn't want to let it eat; it's because he's afraid that if it eats its fill, it will become lazy and unwilling to catch fish for its master anymore. This may have a certain amount of truth to it.

I Curse That Smile of Yours (10)

— Wu Yan

But remembering what Old Liu had just said:

"Not a single Baiyi woman came tonight!"

I went to sleep quietly, even though that smile had made me uncomfortable for quite some time.

The next morning, while I was sweeping horse manure in the stable, I peeked from the sparse shade of the trees toward Old Liu's door. That's terrible! The Baiyi women who had stayed overnight at his shop last night were now appearing one by one under the shade of the mango tree by the door, carrying bamboo baskets. Everyone walked in silence, as if in a funeral procession, with none of the vigor they should have had when setting out in the past. Among them, two Baiyi girls, sixteen or seventeen years old, were even more so hanging their heads low, dragging their feet weakly, as if still showing the signs of weeping from the night before.

I felt very sad, thinking and hoping: I hope that unfortunate thing didn't happen last night! I hope that their unhappiness today is because of a lack of conversation among the female companions, a quarrel, or a hair-pulling fight.

However, before it was time for breakfast, the tragic news that had indeed happened at Old Liu's shop had spread throughout every thatched hut in the valley like the morning breeze.

The boss, while eating, talked about this matter, and then concluded with a mocking tone:

"I wonder how much money that old turtle Liu made last night?... Hmph! That old fellow..."

He shook his head, like a moralistic scholar. He had probably completely forgotten about the matter of begging me last night.

"How wicked and immoral!" The boss's wife said this as soon as she heard the boss speak, and now, after hearing the whole story, she repeated this sigh, and then said: "Fortunately, it didn't happen here. Fortunately... your eyes are blind!" She suddenly saw her little daughter dragging her sleeve in the oily soup while taking tea, and that's how she ended the topic.

"Isn't it all the same?" I thought to myself, but didn't say it. I ate two bowls of rice without tasting anything and quietly walked away.

While sweeping horse manure, I thought sadly: Wasn't I the executioner last night? If it weren't for the old fellow's smile, or if I could have kept my face and not gotten angry, wouldn't things have passed lightly like a game? A heavy brick pressed on my heart.

However, just when I couldn't bear the inner reproach, terrible rumors were added from the outside: Last night, I was the one who led the foreigners to Old Liu's house, and passed on messages for him, threatening the girls who were staying there overnight.

This made me even angrier and more annoyed. Thinking of those rumors that I couldn't explain, and the two weeping, defiled girls, I simply hated Old Liu to the extreme. When I couldn't reduce the pain in my heart, and when I saw people's meaningful smiles, I could only angrily shout:

"Old ghost! I curse that smile of yours!"

Now that I think about it, what a weak and emotional person I was! If I had beaten up that lecherous ghost that night and run back to China, or persisted regardless of ridicule, then my heart would surely be clear and free from filth, and I wouldn't feel any pain now.

Whenever I was troubled by this unpleasant past, besides gnashing my teeth and cursing, "I curse that smile of yours!" I couldn't help but think of those brave and resolute people and say enviously:

"You are blessed!" (The End)

Securities

Slight Dip After Frequent Bond Rises

February Trading Ended Yesterday

Except for 1918 Customs Bonds, All Fell by One to Seven Jiao

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange halted trading in February futures, pending settlement on the 26th. Only March futures were traded on the market for one month. The market initially rose and then retreated, experiencing a slight dip. After the opening rally, prices had risen for four consecutive days. This marks the first sign of fatigue. The overall environment remains sound, but the market price has indeed reached a high level. A temporary retreat is expected. However, based on market sentiment, a sharp decline is unlikely. Prices may still rise initially and then fall. At yesterday's opening, various groups continued to absorb bonds, mostly improving by two or three jiao. Since Jin Duan (short-term bonds) Nos. 4, 30, and 38, etc., were actively sold, market prices reversed from high to low, dropping by three and a half jiao. This caused market sentiment to weaken. The entire Sixth Series also followed suit, falling by two or three jiao. In the second round, many retail longs emerged. Major players continued to sell, but in smaller quantities. Market prices then uniformly declined by two, three, five, or six jiao, mainly because the rampant banditry somewhat dampened bullish sentiment among the general public, with no other factors involved. In the end, market prices, except for 1918 Customs bonds which remained good, rising by three jiao, all fell by one or two to about seven jiao. The total turnover was 6,928,000 yuan, including 3,000 yuan in spot transactions and 6,935,000 yuan in futures. Grains

Biao Flour Has Floating Shorts to Cover

Flour Trading Opens All Day Starting Today

Yesterday in the flour market, after the opening in the morning, prices for each month showed an initial flat and then stable trend. Quotations for foreign wheat, Chicago had no market, Canada recovered by about 0.15 yuan. Therefore, after the opening, the market sentiment for each month remained flat. Subsequently, because various groups covered floating shorts, and manufacturers seemed to reduce dumping, coupled with a slight spot business by the Nanyang group, market sentiment slightly improved. However, foreign wheat still remained loose. For example, Argentine wheat was quoted as low as 4.13 yuan, and manufacturers only offered 4.12 yuan, so there was no transaction. According to the trend of foreign wheat, it is feared that it is still in surplus. As a result, this month rose by 0.005 yuan, March rose by 0.0075 yuan, April rose by 0.015 yuan, May rose by 0.01 yuan, June rose by 0.015 yuan, and July rose by 0.0075 yuan. The Flour Exchange will resume normal trading all day from the 24th. It is heard that the Lantern Festival week will not close even on settlement days.

Factories Continue to Purchase Near-Term Wheat

Yesterday in the wheat market, prices rose consistently in both the morning and afternoon sessions. Due to high prices for futures foreign wheat and sales of spot flour by both Northern and Southern groups, market sentiment improved, and short covering was active. In addition, spot wheat sales were very active, with factories not only purchasing spot wheat but also buying standard near-term months on the exchange. As a result, this month rose by 0.03 yuan, next month rose by 0.02 yuan, and April rose by 0.04 yuan. Distant months had orders for foreign wheat and were new wheat standards, so they were shorted as soon as they opened. At closing, June was down by 0.005 yuan, and July had little activity and no change. Spot Wuhewan wheat opened at 3.389 yuan, Bengbu at 3.32 yuan, and Shandong at 3.47 yuan, totaling 2,100 bags, which were taken in by Fuxin and Fufeng. The market was similar to the previous market.

White Japonica and Thin Paddy Fell by One Jiao Each

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources of goods for various groups were still scarce, only Nos. 15 and 16 (amounting to about 20+ shi). Sales were sluggish, and there was no sign of a turnaround. This is mainly because the New Year has just begun. Recalling the major conclusion of last year, inventory was weak. There should have been a period of excitement after the opening of the red market, but unexpectedly, this year's phenomenon is such that it is truly unexpected. Yesterday, it initially felt good, but by the later market, it became sluggish again. As a result, the Japonica from Sudong and Nangang that was received in this street lacked the strength to stand firm and fell by 0.05 yuan. Other Changbang Japonica and Duyang Tip, etc., were out of stock and had no market. Fortunately, the Southern and Northern groups continued to move 700-800 bags of Qingjiao, Songsi, Fengxian, and Lian evening rice, relying on the scarcity of goods to stabilize the situation. The time for variety transformation has passed, and it is still flat.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, the 23rd and 24th grade goods arrived from various places downstream. Sales of each grade of goods were sluggish, and the market trended further downstream. White Japonica, Yangjian early, and Thin Paddy prices fell by 0.1 yuan. Baiyuan, Yinyuan were flat and tired by a few cents. Bu Jian, Du Jian, and Ke Jian also showed signs of softening.

Ke Xian Demand Strong, Price Falls

Sales Extremely Sluggish

Yesterday, the Ke Xian market situation became even more sluggish. Because the transit goods that were initially loaded at the end of the lunar year have now arrived continuously, coupled with sufficient base inventory, the accumulating goods are increasing, and the cargo owners are seeking to sell more urgently. Yesterday, the appetites of local Ke brokers were weak. In addition to the shipments made by the Fujian group a few days ago, there are still 20,000 bags that have not been loaded, so there is a saying that the inventory will be cleared before further processing. Yesterday, it was only intended to handle 2,000 bags as a formality, but the intention was very slack, and it is feared that the realization of another period of slackness will be required in the future. Ningbo and Guangzhou have imported foreign rice to meet the market, and the appetite is very weak. This street pays attention to the arrival from downstream, and the turnover is also minimal. All rice prices have fallen, especially for medium grades. Hunan oily brown rice is still in a state of virtual softness. The market can only turn around if the price drop causes local customers to sell well, otherwise it may continue to be sluggish.
