Shanghai Daily Supplement

Talk

How Can Such a Political Situation Be Reasonable?

— Rainy Night

The bribery case of Japanese Minister of Education Hatoyama is causing a great uproar, filled with smoke and dust. Therefore, Ichiro Kiyose said, "How can such a political situation be reasonable?"

Because Minister of Education Hatoyama is, after all, a person with status, power, and means, evidence can be suppressed, and the court dares not accept the case. People with status and power are indeed much better off. However, Hatoyama is still embarrassed and intends to resign voluntarily, not wanting to attend the review committee. Although Minister Hatoyama has high skills, there are naturally some things that are difficult to do.

After Ichiro Kiyose filed an impeachment motion in the House of Representatives, he also requested to speak, saying, "According to what Mr. Okamoto said earlier, Mr. Hatoyama, who controls the cultural hub, after all, has committed criminal acts. Hearing about the suppression of evidence is truly shocking." When Kiyose was speaking, members of the Seiyukai party all roared and cursed loudly, causing great disturbance in the parliament. This is truly unreasonable.

Ichiro Kiyose also said, "Minister Hatoyama evades taxes, the Minister of Finance is an advisor to Yasuda Hozen Corporation, how can we trust such a government? It is strange that the negotiation committee of each faction actually refused to submit a motion of no confidence. How can this be reasonable?" While Ichiro Kiyose was speaking eloquently, the parliament was in great turmoil, and Speaker Akita prohibited Kiyose from speaking. This is also truly unreasonable.

From our perspective, what is so rare about Hatoyama, with his personality and position as Minister of Education, engaging in bribery and tax evasion? Why is Kiyose so surprised? The Japanese are, after all, small-minded and lack the attitude of great citizens.

The Four of Us

— Yi Ping

The Four of Us: Different native places, different personalities, by chance we were united. Although we never made a "we don't seek to be born on the same day, but seek to die on the same day" vow, our four spirits have long achieved this step. Since stepping out of the school gates, we have been separated for many times, and last year in Zhenjiang, by another chance, we took a picture together in Boxian Park. This picture reunited us again this year, because more than two and a half of us are unemployed. One day, we talked about the four of us, and with the majority's consent, we believed there was something worth writing about "The Four of Us." Here, I will faithfully and economically write a short profile of each person; even though I am one of the four, I will detach myself from the "I" position and record it purely objectively. Perhaps the reader can discover "your you" in "The Four of Us"!

(1)

The eldest brother is an optimistic, contented, and law-abiding young man. He stepped out of school with his front foot and stepped into the bank with his back foot. He has a good family, and he is content with his position. And the other three of us, unemployment is often chained together, the eldest brother has not experienced the hardship of unemployment; we naturally cannot disturb his peaceful mind with the pain of unemployment. So when one, two, or even three of us visit him, he receives us like ordinary friends, and our conversations are as irrelevant as ordinary friends. It is undeniable that the eldest brother is the most distant among us; the difference in environment has distanced our friendship, that is a fact.

The eldest brother rose from a monthly salary of eight dollars to twenty dollars a month in the bank. He worked diligently to climb up; although he also made meaningless sighs, saying that banking was not a good career, last year, due to some procedural misunderstanding, he claimed to have suffered a loss of more than a thousand dollars. Finally, he switched from that bank to another bank, and then he climbed up again...

(2)

The second eldest is his grandfather's grandson, but not his grandmother's; and even less his mother's son. He has no father.

In the second eldest's hometown, his grandfather was quite famous. The inheritance he left behind, if the second eldest only played mahjong and hung out in teahouses, he could die without knowing how much a copper coin was worth; but he has been drifting in Shanghai for five years, why? Heaven knows!

He worked as a typist in a foreign firm, a low-level clerk in the land bureau, a primary school teacher, and a newspaper reporter, and he could write some not-so-brilliant essays. In five years, he lived a carefree life.

He had many romance stories. In school, "love expert" was constantly attached to his name; but the beginning of his love with his wife was after marriage, and now he is a father.

He inherited his father's lung bacteria and liked to drink even more. He has not had proper rest in five years, so his medical expenses are a regular part of his living expenses, like rent and rice.

He often pretends to be an old man – a young man of twenty-four! He doesn't recall the past, he doesn't yearn for the future, he doesn't cherish the present, he lives, for life.

The second eldest is "I".

(3)

I don't know how to start writing about the third eldest.

His father died, just when we were united by chance; he has a mother who is not his own mother, who depends on him for survival.

After graduation, a father's friend who his parents entrusted him to, took him into his comprador's office. It sounds like he was as fortunate as the eldest brother: stepping out of school with his front foot and stepping into society with his back foot; however, no!

He bit his lower lip and said to us: "$4 a month only." Naturally, he did not inherit any property.

Later he was sent to the north, without an official position, to the comprador's sole-funded branch company. The manager of the branch company thought it necessary to expel him! Anyone would think that he was a guy who didn't know how to go with the flow.

He took a year's superior salary of thirty dollars a month, and was dismissed by the comprador on the grounds of the branch manager's transfer of responsibility. He is still unemployed, but he has to eat every day. In this respect, both he and ordinary people are the same; and there is still a mother who is not his own mother, who depends on him for survival.

(4)

We all say that the fourth eldest is better than us in any way, but the fourth eldest himself does not admit it. As for what he considers "regrettable" (the fourth eldest's catchphrase), I also know it clearly, but I can't write it exceptionally outside the "faithful" scope. In short, it's a lifelong "regret"!

He is an elusive character. From the time we met until now, there has been no slight change in his behavior. He is the inventor of "Taiwan style". He would rather not smoke at all, but if he does, it has to be Capstan. After the January 28th Incident, he switched to smoking White Golden Dragon, he is a patriotic practitioner.

When he is happy, he can spend the only twenty cents in his pocket to go to the Great World. When he is sad, he drinks at the counter instead. If he has a whole ten-dollar bill in his pocket today, he wants us to find a way to spend the money, the more novel the spending, the better.

It's okay to complain about poverty with him, but he just raises his hands and pretends to be Laurel in distress – but no matter what, he can't pretend as well as I do. If we talk about "regret", he wants to drink. If he has no money, he can borrow everywhere, get drunk and cry, and after crying, he feels too bored.

There is another thing that must be mentioned in his life history: when I got married, he almost broke up with me because of the failure of the bridal chamber hazing. I still think it's "regrettable".

This is the four of us!

Quick Sketch of the Jai Alai Court

— Jian

On Avenue Joffre, the red, blue, and green neon lights of the Cathay Theatre, spelling out words, were already swallowing some foreign gentlemen, ladies, and high-class Chinese. Across the street on Avenue Albert, even more cars were parked in front of the jai alai court, and the people entering the jai alai court were as turbulent as a river.

(This jai alai game was originally a Spanish exercise, but later became a form of gambling. In Shanghai, like dog racing, it absorbs the money of a group of gamblers. And these gamblers include merchants, gentlemen, university professors, movie stars, students, and people from all walks of life.)

Inside the iron net, the ball is being played; outside the iron net, the seats are like mountainsides, and people are sitting, standing, smoking, talking, applauding, and boasting like mountains. On both sides, high up, hung blackboards with white words showing the betting odds. People were shouting along with the markings on the board, "Number two has three points!" "Number two has four points. The seat is secure!" "Number five, two points, damn it!"

The whistle blew, the lights in the arena dimmed, the seats lit up, and the noise rose to a boil. "Number two, five points!" Someone shouted happily. Near this person sat a young couple. Hearing this cheer, the man's thin yellow face turned even paler, and he seemed to be cursing someone under his breath, tearing the losing ticket into pieces. Hearing this cheer, the woman's rosy face turned even redder, her eyes staring ahead, and she also tore the waste ticket in her hand.

"I said number two would definitely come tonight, but you wouldn't believe me!" the woman complained, still staring ahead.

"Didn't number five often come last night? What can I do if he doesn't come tonight? Damn it!" the man defended.

"Someone on Avenue Joffre is calling for rickshaws, wanting two. This is a good sign for number two."

"Ugh, you believe in those things!"

As the man spoke, he ordered the servant boy standing next to him waiting for customers to buy tickets, "Number five, win only, two tickets." The woman said, "Number two, a seat." The man said, "Number two won't come." The woman sneered and turned her face to look at the players practicing hitting the ball in the iron net before the game, her eyes shooting at the vigorous body of the Izasu player wearing number two uniform.

Radio music was playing rapidly. The tide of people surged to the ticket counters in the back, and then to the front of the iron net. The whistle blew, the game began. A moment of silence, only the sound of the ball hitting the hard wall, bi bi. The ball hit the floor, number two, one point, then hit the floor again, number two, two points. The third time, the opponent's ball hit the floor again, number two, three points. People's conversation became noisy.

"Number two will definitely come this time," said the person who bought number two tickets, a joyful and triumphant expression on his face, smoking a cigarette.

"Number one is really a rice bucket!" The person who bought number one sighed in hatred, a furious and frustrated expression on his face, throwing the cigarette on the ground and stepping on it.

"Number two, five points!" Someone shouted wildly. Music started, the noise was loud.

Number two won again.

The woman won four dollars and twenty cents for a seat, sneered at the man and said, "Didn't listen to me, has number five come now?" The man said, "You'll see, number five will definitely come this time." The woman snorted from her nostrils and ignored him. The man again ordered the servant boy to buy two tickets for number five to win only. The woman wanted to buy a number two seat, but the man stopped her and said, "Will number two come again this time, silly?" The woman took back the money she had extended, half believing and half doubting.

The whistle blew again, the game started again, and number two was again five points.

The woman immediately stood up, her expression showing a sense of annoyance and contempt towards the man.

"What?"

"Go home!"

"One more game, then leave."

The woman endured, not answering, and sat down. After waiting for a while, she said sharply, aggressively, and concisely,

"Has number five come?"

The man's expression, originally frustrated, immediately turned to disgust and anger when he heard the woman's question, and he threw his cigarette on the ground.

"I'll buy even if he doesn't come!"

The woman sensed that the man's temper was flaring, swallowed her saliva, shrugged her shoulders, rolled her eyes, and endured in silence. The man's temper did not get a response, and instead he spoke softly and ingratiatingly, "What can I do if he doesn't come?" The woman's temper flared up, and she said again sharply, aggressively, and concisely, "Didn't I tell you to buy number two?" The man softened, as if knowing his mistake, and smiled flatteringly at the woman, "I'll definitely buy number two this time, okay?" "If you had listened to me earlier, wouldn't we have won?" The woman also smiled.

Radio music was playing. The tide of people surged back and forth. The whistle blew again. The game started.

The radio music stopped again, and the people's voices also stilled... again the ball was thrown to the salt wall.

"Number three, four points, five points!" The people who bought number three were applauding, this was the only time he came tonight.

The woman, both angry and frustrated, and with a look of deep apology to her husband, said,

"Number two just won't come this time;"

"Let's go back." The man stood up.

The woman looked at her husband with an apologetic expression, and the man stood there looking at his wife's expression, suddenly smiling at her, his anger completely gone, and said, "It's getting late, we still have class tomorrow."

The woman also smiled, put on her coat and followed her husband out of the jai alai court from the crowd.

One of the Arts of Living

— Nai Shuo

No matter which way you look at it, in this world, if you want to live a good life, you must learn to be clever. This is absolutely good, no need to say more reasons.

For example, some people vigorously learn from foreigners to give up their seats to women in first-class trams, while others in third-class trams stare blankly with wide eyes at the women who can't stand steadily and sway back and forth, as if they have completely forgotten the foreign etiquette of giving up seats. I can call these people clever, and the degree of their cleverness is indeed considerable.

Originally, for example, taking foreign etiquette as an example, it is only in those places full of foreign flavor that it can be done vigorously. Otherwise, it is a waste of effort. Shouting "Moreton So" or shaking hands is only effective in front of foreign dignitaries or gentlemen who understand this kind of etiquette. If you grab the hand of an old country man and shake it a few times, or say a few jibberish foreign phrases, he will either suspect that you are joking, or he will suspect that you are scolding him. The result will definitely be a boring experience.

Therefore, people who are generally clever in mind and speech always walk into foreign-style places and practice foreign etiquette. To women who dress in foreign styles, they are like ancestors, as if it is a pleasure and a matter of course to put their butt on their own heads. As for going to third-class trams, they do not hesitate to show that men are kings, and women seem to bring bad luck as soon as they get close to them. So even if people stand until their legs are sore, if there is a place to lean on to sleep, they still have to shamelessly stretch their long legs and sleep.

"Do not speak of the Way to those who are not the right people," is the etiquette of the former kings. To be able to do this under the power of foreign dignitaries, the people are truly rare.

Modern Celebrities' Painting and Calligraphy

— Pang Jun

The river is like a large round mirror reflecting this verdant spiral peak. Since the Qin dynasty, the guardian's spirit spring has connected to Dongting Lake. Bamboo terraces and many mountains meet the mossy steps. Ten thousand cicadas listen to the sigh. The toilers have no way to climb the Buddha's threshold. The Wuyou Temple gradually becomes densely populated with human smoke. Sedan chairs advance unceasingly, saying, "Following the sloping road, descend the mountain and enter the county court." Green, evil bamboo breeds mosquito air, and immortal thatch makes dog shapes. In the morning, three beautiful things are picked, one for making a decaying age. Emei County, record of Emei travels, recognized poem.

Page 22

Page 23

Appreciating the various jealousies of those old spinsters is truly a worldly happiness. Because they always find something ridiculous in others' feelings, they can truly be called people who know how to arrange their own lonely lives.

It is clearly Zhu Meili's lovely flowers, but they deliberately trample on them, only old spinsters can do this. It is clearly a pleasant weather, the best time to throw yourself into the intoxication of a wild outing, but they deliberately curse and insult it, only these old spinsters can do this. They regard love as a sin, and the closeness between men and women as the most unclean behavior in the world, no one but these old spinsters can do this.

These various absurd behaviors, all come from the hands of so-called human beings, which seems strange, but when you think of the fact that even dogs have mad dogs, you don't think there is anything too strange about it. From this, if you reflect and understand it carefully, you may find that this kind of absurd behavior is also an inevitable result of the development of things.

Looking at the fact that old people strictly forbid young people to enjoy themselves to the fullest, it seems that the key to explaining this problem has been found. Like old spinsters, when old people want to carry out their above-mentioned intentions, they always use many ethical and moral terms. Listening to their words, it seems that they are really concerned about young people. But when we press on the true meaning of his words, it is clearly nothing more than a kind of jealousy. Because enjoyment often excludes the elderly, and the victory of love often belongs to young people, but both of these are undeniably desired by the elderly.

Like old people, enjoyment and love are also eagerly sought by old spinsters. However, the result is always being excluded by enjoyment and love. Therefore, thinking that enjoyment can be pursued by everyone, but this is denied by reality, they feel a bad emotion, and in anger, they curse the successful people, which is also a natural fact.

Therefore, thinking of the vixen who scolds the sour grapes because she can't get them, and from this fox turning to this kind of old spinster, if you say that you can't find any fun in it, then you are really not worth talking to.

The Sorrow of a Father's Death

— Qing

"Is your father any better today?" This is what I asked Juan whenever I saw her in the past few days, because she had been frequently asking me for leave to go home early to take care of her father, because her father's condition was deteriorating, and even the doctors had given up hope. I usually knew that Juan's academic performance and character were very satisfactory to me, so I was particularly concerned about everything about her.

"My father passed away at six o'clock this morning." Juan told me with tears in her eyes when I asked her again, "Juan, is your father any better?" "My name has already been registered, but I don't know if I can continue to study next semester, although my eldest aunt's brother always comforts me and says, "Juan, I won't mistreat you in the future." As she said this, tears streamed down her face from the corners of her eyes.

Then, she told me the following: "My mother is nominally in a concubine's position, because ten years ago, my father lost his job, so the family's situation deteriorated. My eldest aunt - my father's first wife - saw that my father was a poor scholar and became disaffected and abandoned my father, taking her own son with her. A year later, my father's business slowly improved and he married my mother. Now I have a brother who is mentally retarded and a younger brother who is still a baby."

Alas! Juan, who is in such a situation, has lost her father, who was the protector of their economy and everything else. Their life from now on is too bleak and miserable! Such a promising person has also lost the gardener who cultivated her! Is this fate?

At this time, the scene of my own father's death also appeared before my eyes. Alas! Juan and I are in the same tragic fate!

If your own mother becomes someone's stepmother, all kinds of troubles and misfortunes will befall us children.

This was something that happened four years ago. The bad news of my father's death came into my ears. After receiving the family report, I rushed home at night for the funeral, because I was drifting at that time. When the sky was dawning, the ship arrived at the port and brought my lonely body back to my hometown. When I knelt before my father's coffin, my heart broke! Alas! My dear and kind father had finally left me and fallen into eternal sleep. Oh! Father, at the ends of the earth, at the edge of the sea, where can I find the father who loved me?

At that time, I still remember my brother comforting me in the same way, saying, "I won't mistreat you." Ah, now, what is the answer in reality?.........

The City God Temple

— Wen Li

Who has not heard of the City God Temple in the city, even if they have never been to Shanghai?

This day was the first day of the Lunar New Year. I heard that the City God Temple in the city was the most lively today, so I strolled on the road and walked into the city. The location of the old city wall on Minguo Road was already crowded with tourists and very lively. Walking into the city near the Little World Amusement Park, there were so many tourists that I was squeezed until I was sweating. Suddenly, I heard the wa-wa sound of a car behind me, and I followed everyone to avoid it under the wall. I saw an old man with a leather collar and black glasses sitting in the car, with a delicate wife shaking next to him. They were visiting the City God Temple by car. I wondered if the car could get in. The policemen on duty waved their sticks and shouted for the tourists to move away, but the road was small and there were many people, so the car's prestige had no way to show off. The old man and wife had to walk. If you walk, I will also walk. The tide of people behind me suddenly surged, pushing and squeezing, and the old man and wife were trapped in the middle, floating and unable to breathe. I thought to myself, today it is impossible to distinguish between the rich and the poor. If you don't want to sweat and be crowded, you'd better step aside and turn back. But the old man and wife were also stubborn, and they followed the crowd onto the Nine-Bend Bridge with smiles. As I squeezed along, I looked at the water under the Nine-Bend Bridge, covered with floating green moss and not clear enough to be used as a mirror, and I felt unhappy. Suddenly, a conflict broke out in front, and people shouted and cursed. I stood high and looked, and it turned out that it was a group of women trapped in the center of the bridge, crowded from front to back, unable to move forward or backward, and arguing with the people in front, back, left, and right. Since the center of the bridge was blocked, we couldn't move forward, but we couldn't retreat either, so everyone stopped, and I also stopped. When I stopped, some memories surfaced in my mind: during the annual God Parade Lantern Festival in my hometown, the miserable scene of women being trapped in the center was really ugly. Those hooligans and rascals would grope them up and down, it was simply animalistic behavior, and the women were humiliated, unable to cry or laugh. I looked up at the women on the Nine-Bend Bridge at this time. Fortunately, although they were trapped in the center, they were still able to shout and curse to clear the crowd and slowly moved forward.

After entering the main hall of the City God Temple, the incense smoke made it difficult for me to open my eyes. Unable to see clearly, I had to follow the crowd out of the front hall and squeeze out onto the street in front of the temple. There were many people selling toys and spinning tops on the street, especially one cheap jewelry store where the man calling out to sell had pearl pendants hanging from his ears, a fake diamond necklace around his neck, and jewelry-like rings on his hands, truly a walking advertisement. I turned around to the street selling birdcages. Spring had not yet arrived, and I didn't hear any birdsong, only cages. The tide of people was just surging. I was sweating too much on my back, and my mouth was a little thirsty. I looked up and saw a glutinous rice ball shop on the side of the road. I rushed forward to eat a bowl of glutinous rice balls. The shop was also full of people. I don't know if it was because I was hungry, but the glutinous rice balls were very delicious. People say that the glutinous rice balls in the City God Temple are famous, and I might be lucky today. After leaving the glutinous rice ball shop, I followed the tide of people out again. Along the way, there were people selling flower lanterns and balloons, all red and green. If I had a child at home, I would definitely buy him one or two flower lanterns. Squeezing onto Minguo Road, there were fewer tourists, and I finally took a breath and walked comfortably home.

The Biggest Hope

— Dai Ni

The diaries I’ve written over the past five years have piled up into several thick volumes. At the beginning of each year, I always write down many beautiful hopes, like a preacher. But when I settle the accounts at the end of the year, I am greatly shocked. It is true that only with hope can you feel the disappointment afterwards. If you live a muddled life like Spring, you probably won’t feel sadness. But I am a person with a brain and thoughts. I know I am deceiving myself, but I will continue to deceive myself year after year until I die.

Now it is the New Year again, the beginning of my sixth year of wandering. Somewhat following my principle of deceiving myself, I write down a few words of hope. However, the quality of these hopeful words has been decreasing year by year. This year, I really can't repeat the kind of hope I had before, because it has given me too much disappointment. So, I avoid the important and dwell on the trivial, leaving some ink marks at the beginning of my diary.

I seem to feel that I am always working hard all day long, physically and mentally, squeezing myself dry. I am worth next to nothing if I were to be auctioned off. Of course, pig buyers choose the strong ones. Regarding this sick body of mine, I want to hope for a great turnaround. My friends who know me know that I go to the doctor for injections every other day. If the needle marks could be left permanently, there wouldn’t be a single piece of clean skin left on my two arms. But it's still useless. I am getting thinner day by day, year by year. I have even fantasized about how thin a person can actually become, and I am using myself as a test subject to see how thin I can get. However, I can't, because even if I don't eat, it doesn't matter, but my wife and children can't go without food. To earn a living, I have to work. So, I get more injections, preparing my body for the day someone will buy it.

Therefore, my biggest hope this year is to be able to lie quietly in a hospital for three months, or even a year, and use scientific methods to increase my weight (the most important thing to declare is that I am not afraid of death because of my thinness; God knows that). However, the biggest problem is that I have never seen a doctor who has the heart to cut a piece of his own flesh to give to me, or who would pay for my medical expenses out of his own pocket. Money, money, money, it twirled around in front of me for a long time. I chose the safest way, buying an aviation lottery ticket. It's a kind of gambling that won’t kill you like smoking or tossing dice, and the "hope" afterwards is endless.

Now I am waiting, waiting for March 2nd to arrive quickly. If readers don’t see Dai Ni's money-making manuscripts in the future, it means he has entered the hospital. He plans to get stronger before being auctioned off again. If any readers want to make this deal, please also hope that I win the fourth aviation lottery.

Amateur Mailbox

Answers to Several Legal Questions (I)

Editor:

As a young and inexperienced person, I naturally have many things I do not understand about the world. Now I am writing down several questions that are lingering in my mind and that I urgently need to resolve, and I ask you to answer them. I believe that a kind and motherly gentleman like yourself will be able to answer me!

1. My aunt has no son, so ten years ago, she adopted someone else's son. Later, she wanted to raise her own daughter, so she drove the other son away in every possible way. The son, unable to bear the pain, finally returned to his mother's home. However, this son wore mourning for my aunt's parents-in-law when they died, which is customary for a filial grandson. In this case, can this son have the right to inherit the estate?

2. If the son-in-law of my aunt comes to take over the household and inherit, can he change his original surname? Can close relatives refuse him? Does he have the right to inherit the estate?

Sir: You are the needle pointing south for young people. Please answer the above two questions sincerely! With this I await your reply, and wish you peace. Sincerely, Zhang Peng

Editor's Note:

(1) Adoptive parents can terminate the adoption relationship with their adopted children. According to the law, it should be done in writing. According to what is stated in the letter, the adoption relationship is still in effect, so the adopted son has the right to inherit the estate. However, his share should be half that of a biological child. Also, pay attention to the month and year of the death of the aunt's husband, because only if the death occurred after 1927 does the daughter have the right to inherit.

(2) Although close relatives cannot object to the son-in-law taking over the household, he does not have the right to inherit the estate.

Novel

Husband and Wife (7)

— Yu Mei

"It's alright, you go in. Be careful of the wind."

Third Sister laughed inwardly, pushed open the door, placed the lamp on the table, turned over the fire in the brazier inside the fire bucket by the table, and then climbed in, shrinking her whole body together. She looked at the lamplight on the bed, thinking about some past events whose timing had been lost. Her shadow was reflected on the wall, blurred. Her shadow had been reflected on this wall for many years. Although her strong needs in life had never been suppressed, although countless kisses and countless touches had adorned her flourishing years, although she had worn clothes that made men feel willing to serve her, the concrete expression of her life in terms of food, clothing, and shelter was, as she herself understood, not good. Although she had engaged in behavior that violated determinism, her thoughts were deterministic. Her husband was a decorative item in her life. She knew that she would not have the fate to become rich, but she often hoped that she would have a full box of banknotes.

Everything was unusually quiet. There was the sound of gongs and drums in the distance. This sound aroused her nostalgia. The happy and glorious expression she had when she heard this sound many years ago was reflected in her mind. Now, she felt that the sound of the gongs only highlighted her desolation and aging, but everything in the past was blurred. A slight breeze rustled on the low roof ridge. She pulled her head in even tighter.

After a while, the front door rang. Footsteps were approaching. The familiar sound of footsteps made her ears perk up. She hurriedly took the foreign coins from the opium tray in her hand, put them away, and climbed back into the fire bucket. She asked,

"Why are you running back at this hour?"

Xu San, who had originally wanted to come home to rest for the night, suddenly didn't know how to answer. He stammered, "Just coming home to take a look."

He had already walked into the room. He put on a smiling face, looked at his wife's lifeless appearance, and asked,

"Did you lose any money?" He still had a smile on his lips.

"No. How can I always let people lose money?" Third Sister said listlessly, lowering her head again.

"Hmph." Xu San grunted, swallowing the words he wanted to say. He stood next to his wife, wanting to change the atmosphere.

"These two days are the New Year, and you don't even think about making a little more business at the gambling den. Has the ash come out yet?"

"The ash has all come out. At the gambling den." The husband knew that even his miserable work could not be fully enjoyed.

"I have a bit of a headache tonight." She stroked her forehead with her hand. She had eliminated all of his expectations.

"Oh." Xu San expressed his comforting thoughts with a single "Oh." He was silent.

"Take some more cigarettes with you, it's good to make a little more business while you can."

"I don't want to go tonight. I've been working myself to death these past two days. I haven't had a good night's sleep."

"When are you going to be busy if not these two days? Maybe someone will come to smoke tonight. These two days, people are very busy talking and confiding. My headache is like being split with a knife. I might even have to serve people late into the night tonight."

Xu San had nothing more to say. Third Sister wanted him to go up to the gambling den to do a little more business no matter what, giving him many packs of cigarettes. She herself, without any energy, returned to squatting on the fire bucket. Xu San lingered for a moment, believing that her old illness had recurred, and then staggered out of the room. She lazily said,

"Close the door tightly."

Home
